# LoCoBench-Agent Task

## Task Information

**Task ID**: rust_web_social_expert_073_architectural_understanding_expert_01
**Category**: architectural_understanding
**Difficulty**: expert
**Language**: rust
**Context Length**: 1064755 tokens
**Files**: 88

## Task Title

Architectural Analysis for Real-time Feature Integration in an Event-Driven System

## Description

EduPulse Live is a complex, event-driven social learning platform built in Rust. The system architecture is highly modularized to handle features like user authentication, study group management, content searching, and session management. The source code is spread across numerous modules with non-descriptive names (e.g., `module_1.txt`, `module_2.txt`), requiring deep code analysis to understand their purpose. The core of the system relies on an event bus for communication between components, following patterns like CQRS (Command Query Responsibility Segregation). The company now wants to introduce a highly interactive 'Real-time Collaborative Whiteboard' feature for study groups. As a senior architect, your task is to analyze the existing architecture to determine the best integration strategy and identify potential challenges.

## Your Task

Your task is to perform a thorough architectural analysis and create a strategic plan for integrating a new 'Real-time Collaborative Whiteboard' feature. You must not write any implementation code. Your response should be a detailed report based on your understanding of the existing codebase.

1.  **Identify Core Architectural Components:** Analyze the provided files (`config.txt`, `package.json`, and `src/module_*.txt` files) to identify and describe the roles of the key components in the existing event-processing pipeline. Specifically, identify the modules responsible for:
    *   API Gateway / Handling incoming HTTP requests.
    *   User Authentication and Session Management.
    *   Publishing commands/events to the message bus.
    *   Consuming events to update data stores (write models).
    *   Serving read-optimized data (query models).

2.  **Trace an Existing Data Flow:** Describe the complete lifecycle of a user creating a new post in a study group. Trace this action from the initial API call through the event bus to the final data persistence, naming the specific modules (`module_XX.txt`) involved at each stage.

3.  **Propose an Integration Strategy:** Design a high-level architectural solution for the 'Real-time Collaborative Whiteboard' feature. Your proposal must address:
    *   The mechanism for handling low-latency, real-time communication (e.g., drawing actions) between clients.
    *   The new service(s) or module(s) required.
    *   How whiteboard state will be persisted without compromising the performance of the core application.
    *   How the new feature will integrate with the existing user authentication and event bus.

4.  **Visualize the Architecture:** Generate two diagrams in MermaidJS `graph TD` format:
    *   **Diagram 1:** The existing architecture, showing the flow you traced in step 2.
    *   **Diagram 2:** The proposed architecture, incorporating the new Collaborative Whiteboard components.

5.  **Identify Architectural Risks:** List and explain the top 3 potential architectural risks or bottlenecks associated with your proposed integration. Focus on performance, scalability, and data consistency.

## Expected Approach

An expert developer would start by examining configuration and dependency files for high-level clues, then dive into the source code to confirm hypotheses and map out the system.

1.  **Initial Reconnaissance:** The developer would first inspect `package.json` to identify key dependencies like `axum` (web framework), `tokio` (async runtime), `sqlx` (database), `serde` (serialization), and a message bus client like `nats` or `lapin` (for RabbitMQ). They would then check `src/config.txt` for service URLs (e.g., NATS server address, multiple database connection strings suggesting CQRS), secret keys, and other configuration that defines the environment.

2.  **Pattern Identification:** The developer would scan the `src/module_*.txt` files for recurring patterns and keywords. They would look for `axum::Router` to find the API entry points, structs with `#[derive(Serialize, Deserialize)]` that look like `Events` or `Commands`, functions that `publish` to a message bus, and functions that `subscribe` or `handle` messages. This helps categorize the opaque modules.

3.  **Component Mapping:** By combining clues from dependencies and code patterns, the developer would map modules to roles. For example, a module that sets up an `axum::Router` and calls an authentication function is likely the API Gateway. Modules with functions that handle structs named `CreatePostCommand` are command handlers. Modules that handle `PostCreatedEvent` and perform `sqlx` database writes are event consumers/denormalizers.

4.  **Tracing and Diagramming:** The developer would trace a specific command, like creating a post, by finding the API endpoint, seeing which command it generates, finding the handler for that command, seeing which event the handler emits, and finally finding the consumer for that event. This flow would be translated into a MermaidJS diagram.

5.  **Solution Design:** For the new feature, the expert would recognize that standard event bus patterns are too high-latency for real-time drawing. They would propose a dedicated WebSocket service. This service would handle the WebSocket connections, broadcasting drawing data directly to clients in a specific 'room' or 'session'. For persistence, they would suggest snapshotting the whiteboard state to the primary database periodically, while perhaps using a faster cache like Redis for transient actions. This new service would still hook into the main event bus for authentication and to be notified when a study session starts or ends.

## Evaluation Criteria

- **Component Identification Accuracy:** How accurately did the agent identify the roles of the key modules (`module_1`, `module_15`, `module_68`, `module_4`, etc.) based on code analysis?
- **Architectural Pattern Recognition:** Did the agent correctly identify the high-level patterns in use, specifically Event-Driven Architecture and CQRS, citing evidence like separate DB URLs or command/event naming?
- **Data Flow Analysis:** Was the agent's trace of the 'Create Post' flow logical and did it reference the correct sequence of component interactions (API -> Command -> Handler -> Event -> Consumer)?
- **Proposed Solution Viability:** Is the proposed architecture for the whiteboard feature sound? Does it correctly identify WebSockets as the appropriate technology and propose a reasonable strategy for state management and persistence?
- **Visualization Quality:** Are the MermaidJS diagrams syntactically correct, clear, and do they accurately represent both the existing and proposed architectures as described in the analysis?
- **Risk Assessment Insight:** Are the identified risks relevant to the proposed architecture? Does the explanation demonstrate a deep understanding of the trade-offs in distributed, real-time systems (e.g., stateful vs. stateless services, consistency vs. performance)?

     1→```rust
     2→//! src/module_4.rs
     3→//!
     4→//! Centralised domain-event infrastructure for EduPulse Live.
     5→//!
     6→//! This module exposes:
     7→//!   * DomainEvent & DomainEventKind – strongly-typed, versioned event
     8→//!     definitions shared across bounded contexts.
     9→//!   * EventPublisher – service-layer abstraction allowing the core API to
    10→//!     remain ignorant of transport details (NATS, Kafka, etc.).
    11→//!   * NatsEventPublisher – production implementation that publishes JSON
    12→//!     envelopes to a NATS JetStream subject hierarchy.
    13→//!   * EventStore – ACID append-only persistence used for audit trail / GDPR
    14→//!     erase workflow.
    15→//!   * PostgresEventStore – repository implementation via `sqlx`.
    16→//!   * LearningPulseService – sample use-case that persists a new learning
    17→//!     pulse and emits the corresponding event within a single transaction.

     1→```rust
     2→//! src/module_50.rs
     3→//!
     4→//! Reliable Domain Event Outbox implementation
     5→//! ===========================================
     6→//! This module provides a production-ready* implementation of the
     7→//! Outbox/Inbox pattern for EduPulse Live.  All domain events are first
     8→//! persisted inside the same Postgres transaction that modified the
     9→//! aggregate and are later *atomically* published to the message broker
    10→//! (e.g. RabbitMQ).  This guarantees *at-least-once* delivery without
    11→//! sacrificing database consistency.
    12→//!
    13→//! # Architecture
    14→//! 1. Domain layer inserts a row into the `outbox_events` table
    15→//!    through [`OutboxRepository::insert`].
    16→//! 2. [`OutboxProcessor`] polls the table on an interval (or is triggered
    17→//!    by NOTIFY/LISTEN) and publishes unpublished events.
    18→//! 3. After a successful publish it marks the event as `published_at`.
    19→//!
    20→//! # Usage
    21→//! ```no_run
    22→//! #[tokio::main]
    23→//! async fn main() -> anyhow::Result<()> {
    24→//!     env_logger::init();
    25→//!
    26→//!     let db = PgPoolOptions::new()
    27→//!         .max_connections(5)
    28→//!         .connect("postgres://user:password@localhost/edupulse")
    29→//!         .await?;
    30→//!
    31→//!     // Initialise AMQP connection
    32→//!     let amqp_addr = "amqp://guest:guest@127.0.0.1:5672/%2f";
    33→//!     let publisher = RabbitMqPublisher::connect(amqp_addr, "edupulse.events").await?;
    34→//!
    35→//!     // Fire-and-forget background processing task
    36→//!     OutboxProcessor::spawn(db.clone(), publisher);
    37→//!
    38→//!     // … start REST API, etc.
    39→//!     Ok(())
    40→//! }
    41→//
... (truncated)

I have completed the architectural analysis for the EduPulse Live platform. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Analysis Complete

I thoroughly analyzed the EduPulse Live codebase and produced a comprehensive architectural report at `/logs/agent/solution.md`.

### Key Findings:

1. **Core Architecture Identified:**
   - **Event-Driven Architecture (EDA)** with NATS JetStream, RabbitMQ, and Kafka support
   - **CQRS Pattern** - Separate write (PostgreSQL) and read (Elasticsearch) models
   - **Outbox Pattern** - Reliable at-least-once event delivery

2. **Key Module Mappings:**
   - `module_1.txt` - Authentication & Session Management (JWT + Redis)
   - `module_4.txt`, `module_9.txt` - Event Publishing Infrastructure
   - `module_33.txt`, `module_81.txt` - Domain Service Layer (Command Handlers)
   - `module_15.txt`, `module_27.txt` - Event Consumers (Read Model Projections)

3. **Data Flow Traced:**
   - Complete lifecycle from HTTP request → Auth validation → Command handling → Event publishing → Consumer processing

4. **Whiteboard Integration Proposal:**
   - WebSocket Gateway for real-time communication (<20ms latency)
   - CRDT-based state management for conflict-free collaboration
   - Dual-path architecture: Redis Pub/Sub (hot path) + Event Bus (cold path)
   - Tiered persistence: Redis → PostgreSQL → S3

5. **Top 3 Architectural Risks:**
   - WebSocket session statefulness and horizontal scaling
   - Real-time latency vs. event bus mismatch
   - Data consistency between ephemeral and persistent state

The solution includes two MermaidJS diagrams showing both the existing architecture and the proposed architecture with the Collaborative Whiteboard components integrated.

Although placed in `src/config.txt` by convention of this task,\n//! this file contains Rust source code that can be `include!`-d or\n//! copied into a proper `config.rs` module. The implementation uses the `config` crate to merge multiple\n//! sources in the following precedence (highest \u21a0 lowest):\n//!   1. All structures derive `Deserialize` and are therefore _data-\n//! driven_; callers only need to care about the resulting strongly\n//! typed `AppConfig` object.\n//\n// ---------------------------------------------------------------\n//! Example \u2935\ufe0f  (`default.yaml` sitting next to the binary):\n//!\n//! ```yaml\n//! environment: \"production\"\n//! database:\n//!   driver: \"postgres\"\n//!   url: path::Path};\n\nuse config::{builder::DefaultState, Config, ConfigBuilder, Environment, File};\nuse serde::Deserialize;\n\n/// A convenience alias for the error type exposed by the `config` crate.\npub type ConfigError = config::ConfigError;\n\n/// Database connectivity and pooling parameters.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Deserialize)]\npub struct DatabaseConfig {\n    pub driver: String,\n    pub url: String,\n    pub pool_size: u32,\n}\n\n/// AMQP / message-broker settings.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Deserialize)]\npub struct BrokerConfig {\n    pub host: String,\n    pub port: u16,\n    pub username: String,\n    pub password: String,\n    pub vhost: String,\n    pub heartbeat_secs: u64,\n}\n\n/// Authentication and authorization settings (JWT, OAuth, etc.).\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Deserialize)]\npub struct AuthConfig {\n    /// Symmetric key used to sign/verify JWTs (HS256).\n    pub jwt_secret: String,\n    /// Short-lived access token in minutes.\n    pub token_lifetime_minutes: u32,\n    /// Bcrypt cost factor for hashing passwords.\n    pub password_salt_cost: u8,\n\n    /// Optional OAuth registration for Google.\n    pub oauth_google_client_id: Option<String>,\n    pub oauth_google_client_secret: Option<String>,\n\n    /// Optional OAuth registration for Microsoft EDU.\n    pub oauth_microsoft_client_id: Option<String>,\n    pub oauth_microsoft_client_secret: Option<String>,\n}\n\n/// Public HTTP server and TLS termination layer configuration.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Deserialize)]\npub struct ServerConfig {\n    pub listen_addr: String,\n    pub tls_cert_path: String,\n    pub tls_key_path: String,\n\n    /// CORS origins allowed to access the API.\n    pub allowed_origins: Vec<String>,\n\n    /// 32-byte key used for encrypting server-side sessions.\n    pub session_key: String,\n\n    /// Redis connection string (scheme://host:port/db).\n    pub redis_uri: String,\n    /// Sliding expiration for session elasticsearch_url: String,\n    pub index_prefix: String,\n    pub batch_size: u16,\n}\n\n/// Top-level strongly typed application configuration object.\n///\n/// All nested fields are flattened from the merged configuration\n/// sources and validated by `serde`.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Deserialize)]\npub struct AppConfig {\n    pub environment: String,\n    pub database: DatabaseConfig,\n    pub broker: BrokerConfig,\n    pub auth: AuthConfig,\n    pub server: ServerConfig,\n    pub search: SearchConfig,\n}\n\nimpl AppConfig {\n    /// Build an `AppConfig` from layered sources.\n    ///\n    /// `base_path` \u2013 directory containing `default.*` / `local.*` files.\n    /// `env_prefix` \u2013 environment variable prefix (e.g. `\"EDUPULSE\"`).\n    ///\n    /// # Errors\n    ///\n    /// Returns `ConfigError` when reading or (de)serializing fails.\n    pub fn from_sources<P: AsRef<Path>>(\n        base_path: P,\n        env_prefix: &str,\n    ) -> Result<Self, ConfigError> {\n        let mut builder = Config::builder();\n\n        // --- 1. Files on disk ------------------------------------------------\n        // Accepted extensions: json, toml, yaml, ron, etc.\n        for name in &[\"default\", \"local\"] {\n            // Note: `required(false)` allows the file to be missing silently.\n            builder = builder.add_source(\n                File::with_name(\n                    base_path\n                        .as_ref()\n                        .join(name)\n                        .to_str()\n                        .ok_or_else(|| ConfigError::Foreign(Box::new(\n                            std::io::Error::new(\n                                std::io::ErrorKind::InvalidInput,\n                                \"Non-UTF8 file path in configuration\",\n                            ),\n                        )))?,\n                )\n                .required(false),\n            );\n        }\n\n        // --- 2. Environment variables ---------------------------------------\n        //\n        //   `EDUPULSE_DATABASE__URL=postgres://...` maps to\n        //   `database.url`  (double underscore \u21d2 nested field)\n        builder = builder.add_source(\n            Environment::with_prefix(env_prefix)\n                .separator(\"__\")\n                .try_parsing(true)\n                .list_separator(\",\"),\n        );\n\n        // --------------------------------------------------------------------\n        builder.build()?.try_deserialize::<AppConfig>()\n    }\n}\n\n// ---------------------------------------------------------------\n//! Sanity tests \u2013 `cargo test -p <crate> --lib config`\n// ---------------------------------------------------------------\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n    use std::env;\n\n    /// Ensure we can load configuration from synthetic sources.\n    #[test]\n    fn smoke_loads_from_defaults() {\n        // Place temporary config files in a temp-dir.\n        let dir = tempfile::tempdir().expect(\"tmpdir\");\n\n        std::fs::write(\n            dir.path().join(\"default.yaml\"),\n            r#\"\n            environment: \"test\"\n            database: { driver: Duration::hours(12),\n            argon2: Argon2::default(),\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Registers a new user, returning a newly minted [`Session`] on success.\n    pub async fn register_user(&self, new_user: NewUser) -> Result<Session> {\n        if self.repo.find_by_email(&new_user.email).await?.is_some() {\n            return Err(AuthError::InvalidCredentials); // simplified: email already taken\n        }\n\n        let salt = SaltString::generate(&mut rand::thread_rng());\n        let password_hash = self\n            .argon2\n            .hash_password(new_user.password.as_bytes(), &salt)?\n            .to_string();\n\n        let user = User {\n            id: Uuid::new_v4(),\n            email: new_user.email,\n            password_hash,\n            created_at: Utc::now(),\n        };\n\n        self.repo.insert(&user).await?;\n        self.event_bus\n            .publish(&DomainEvent::UserRegistered {\n                user_id: user.id,\n                email: user.email.clone(),\n            })\n            .await?;\n\n        let session = self.create_session(user.id).await?;\n        Ok(session)\n    }\n\n    /// Authenticates a user and returns a valid session token.\n    pub async fn login_user(&self, email: &str, password: &str) -> Result<Session> {\n        let user = self\n            .repo\n            .find_by_email(email)\n            .await?\n            .ok_or(AuthError::InvalidCredentials)?;\n\n        // Verify password\n        let parsed_hash = PasswordHash::new(&user.password_hash)?;\n        self.argon2\n            .verify_password(password.as_bytes(), &parsed_hash)\n            .map_err(|_| AuthError::InvalidCredentials)?;\n\n        let session = self.create_session(user.id).await?;\n\n        self.event_bus\n            .publish(&DomainEvent::UserLoggedIn { user_id: user.id })\n            .await?;\n\n        Ok(session)\n    }\n\n    /// Invalidates an existing session.\n    pub async fn    }\n\n    /// Helper: create a JWT token + Redis cache entry.\n    async fn create_session(&self, user_id: Uuid) -> Result<Session> {\n        let now = Utc::now();\n        let exp = (now + self.session_ttl).timestamp() as usize;\n\n        let claims = Claims {\n            sub: user_id.to_string(),\n            exp,\n            iat: now.timestamp() as usize,\n        };\n\n        let embedded in it.\n    pub async fn validate_token(&self, token: &str) -> Result<Uuid> {\n        // 1. Verify signature / expiration\n        let TokenData { claims, .. } = decode::<Claims>(\n            token,\n            &DecodingKey::from_secret(self.jwt_secret.as_bytes()),\n            &Validation::default(),\n        )?;\n\n        // 2. Check server-side revocation list (Redis)\n        if self\n            .session_store\n            .get_user_id(token)\n            .await\n            .map_err(|e| AuthError::EventBus(e.into()))?\n            .is_none()\n        {\n            return Err(AuthError::InvalidCredentials);\n        }\n\n        let uuid = Uuid::parse_str(&claims.sub).map_err(|_| AuthError::InvalidCredentials)?;\n        Ok(uuid)\n    }\n}\n\n/// =============================================================================================\n/// REST handler glue (simplified for brevity). Here we show just enough to demonstrate SVC integration.\n/// =============================================================================================\n#[cfg(feature = \"rest_api\")]\npub mod std::sync::Arc;\n\n    #[derive(Clone)]\n    pub struct AppState<A> {\n        pub auth_service: Arc<A>,\n    }\n\n    pub fn router<A: 'static + Send + Sync>(\n        state: AppState<A>,\n    ) ->      }\n\n        async fn login(&self, email: &str, password: &str) -> Result<Session> {\n            self.login_user(email, password).await\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Extension(state): Extension<AppState<A>>,\n    ) -> impl IntoResponse\n    where\n        A: AuthServiceTrait,\n    {\n        match state.auth_service.register(payload).await {\n            Ok(session) => (StatusCode::CREATED, Json(session)).into_response(),\n            Err(e) => {\n                error!(\"registration error: {e}\");\n                (StatusCode::BAD_REQUEST, An event\u2013driven badge\u2013awarding micro-service for the\n//! \u201cEduPulse Live \u2013 Event-Driven Social Learning Hub\u201d platform.\n//!\n//! This module demonstrates how the core application publishes\n//! domain events while an out-of-process, autonomous component\n//! (here: `BadgeAwardService`) consumes them, performs business\n//! logic, persists the result and publishes its own follow-up\n//! events.  \n//!\n//! The service is completely self-contained: it hosts an in-memory\n//! dispatcher for local development, yet persists events and state\n//! in Postgres so it can be moved into a distributed setting\n//! later on (e.g. with NATS/Kafka\u2010backed `Dispatcher`).\n//!\n//! Architectural patterns shown here:\n//!   \u2022 Repository Pattern      \u2013 decoupling persistence\n//!   \u2022 Service Layer           \u2013 `BadgeAwardService`\n//!   \u2022 Event Sourcing          \u2013 immutable `EventStore`\n//!   \u2022 Async Rust w/ Tokio     \u2013 non-blocking I/O\n//!   \u2022 Error Handling w/ thiserror + anyhow\n//!\n//! NOTE: In a real-world project this module would be split\n//! into several files/crates.  Everything is co-located here only\n//! to satisfy the single-file constraint of the exercise.\n\nuse std::{\n    collections::HashSet,\n    sync::Arc,\n    time::Duration,\n};\n\nuse async_trait::async_trait;\nuse chrono::{DateTime, Utc};\nuse serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};\nuse sqlx::{postgres::PgPoolOptions, PgPool};\nuse thiserror::Error;\nuse tokio::{\n    select,\n    sync::{broadcast, mpsc, RwLock},\n    task::JoinHandle,\n};\nuse uuid::Uuid;\n\n/// Domain events which can be emitted by EduPulse services.\n///\n/// IMPORTANT: New variants **must** implement `Serialize`/`Deserialize`\n/// so they can be persisted in the event store.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\n#[serde(tag = \"type\", content = \"payload\")]\npub enum DomainEvent {\n    QuizSubmitted(QuizSubmitted),\n    BadgeAwarded(BadgeAwarded),\n    // \u2026 more variants omitted for brevity\n}\n\nimpl DomainEvent {\n    /// Helper returning event name for logging / metrics.\n    pub fn name(&self) -> &'static str {\n        match self {\n            DomainEvent::QuizSubmitted(_) => \"QuizSubmitted\",\n            DomainEvent::BadgeAwarded(_) => \"BadgeAwarded\",\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Metadata common to all envelopes\u2014separates immutable event data\n/// from peripheral transport concerns such as IDs and timestamps.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct EventEnvelope {\n    pub id: Uuid,\n    pub occurred_at: DateTime<Utc>,\n    pub event: DomainEvent,\n}\n\nimpl EventEnvelope {\n    pub fn new(event: DomainEvent) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            id: Uuid::new_v4(),\n            occurred_at: Utc::now(),\n            event,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Event data triggered when a learner submits a quiz.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct QuizSubmitted {\n    pub quiz_id: Uuid,\n    pub learner_id: Uuid,\n    pub score: f32,\n}\n\n/// Event data emitted once the learner qualifies for a badge.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct BadgeAwarded {\n    pub badge_id: Uuid,\n    pub learner_id: Uuid,\n    pub awarded_at: DateTime<Utc>,\n    pub reason: String,\n}\n\n/// Central event dispatcher.  \n/// Internally uses a Tokio broadcast channel so any number of\n/// in-process consumers can receive events concurrently.\n///\n/// In production you might replace the implementation with NATS,\n/// Kafka, RabbitMQ\u2026 etc., leaving the public API intact.\n#[derive(Clone)]\npub struct Dispatcher {\n    sender: broadcast::Sender<EventEnvelope>,\n}\n\nimpl Dispatcher {\n    /// Create a new dispatcher with a configurable ring buffer size.\n    pub fn new(channel_size: usize) -> Self {\n        let (sender, _rx) = broadcast::channel(channel_size);\n        Self { sender }\n    }\n\n    /// Publish an envelope to all subscribers.\n    pub async fn publish(&self, envelope: EventEnvelope) {\n        // broadcast::Sender::send is synchronous but inexpensive.\n        // Failure only occurs when there are no active receivers;\n        // still, we ignore that because the event is persisted in\n        // the store before reaching this point.\n        let _ = self.sender.send(envelope);\n    }\n\n    /// Subscribe to a continuous stream of events.\n    pub fn subscribe(&self) -> broadcast::Receiver<EventEnvelope> {\n        self.sender.subscribe()\n    }\n}\n\n/// Persisted event stream; provides idempotent append + read access.\n/// Uses Postgres JSONB for flexible schema evolution.\n///\n/// Table DDL (run via migrations):\n/// ```sql\n/// CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS event_store (\n///     id           UUID PRIMARY KEY,\n///     occurred_at  TIMESTAMP WITH TIME ZONE NOT NULL,\n///     event_name   TEXT NOT NULL,\n///     payload      JSONB NOT NULL\n/// );\n/// ```\npub struct EventStore {\n    pool: PgPool,\n}\n\nimpl EventStore {\n    pub async fn new(db_url: &str, max_connections: u32) -> Result<Self, sqlx::Error> {\n        let pool = PgPoolOptions::new()\n            .max_connections(max_connections)\n            .connect(db_url)\n            .await?;\n        Ok(Self { pool })\n    }\n\n    /// Append envelope to store.\n    pub async fn append(&self, env: &EventEnvelope) -> Result<(), sqlx::Error> {\n        sqlx::query!(\n            r#\"\n            INSERT INTO event_store (id, occurred_at, event_name, payload)\n            VALUES ($1, $2, $3, $4)\n            \"#,\n            env.id,\n            env.occurred_at,\n            env.event.name(),\n            serde_json::to_value(&env.event)?\n        )\n        .execute(&self.pool)\n        .await?;\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    /// Read events by name\u2014useful for rebuilding read models.\n    pub async fn load_by_event(\n        &self,\n        event_name: &str,\n    ) -> Result<Vec<EventEnvelope>, sqlx::Error> {\n        let recs = sqlx::query!(\n            r#\"\n            SELECT id, occurred_at, payload\n            FROM event_store\n            WHERE event_name = $1\n            ORDER BY occurred_at ASC\n            \"#,\n            event_name\n        )\n        .fetch_all(&self.pool)\n        .await?;\n\n        recs.into_iter()\n            .map(|r| {\n                let event = match event_name {\n                    \"QuizSubmitted\" => DomainEvent::QuizSubmitted(\n                        serde_json::from_value(r.payload)?,\n                    ),\n                    \"BadgeAwarded\" => DomainEvent::BadgeAwarded(\n                        serde_json::from_value(r.payload)?,\n                    ),\n                    _ => unreachable!(\"Unknown event stored in DB\"),\n                };\n                Ok(EventEnvelope {\n                    id: r.id,\n                    occurred_at: r.occurred_at,\n                    event,\n                })\n            })\n            .collect()\n    }\n}\n\n/// Error type covering all repository/service error cases.\n#[derive(Error, Debug)]\npub enum ServiceError {\n    #[error(\"Database error: {0}\")]\n    Database(#[from] sqlx::Error),\n\n    #[error(\"Event serialisation error: {0}\")]\n    Serde(#[from] serde_json::Error),\n\n    #[error(\"Internal channel closed\")]\n    ChannelClosed,\n}\n\n/// Repository abstraction for badge persistence.\n#[async_trait]\npub trait BadgeRepository: Send + Sync {\n    async fn learner_already_has_badge(\n        &self,\n        learner_id: Uuid,\n        badge_id: Uuid,\n    ) -> Result<bool, ServiceError>;\n\n    async fn assign_badge(\n        &self,\n        learner_id: Uuid,\n        badge: &BadgeAwarded,\n    ) -> Result<(), ServiceError>;\n}\n\n/// Postgres-based implementation of the `BadgeRepository`.\n///\n/// Table DDL:\n/// ```sql\n/// CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS learner_badges (\n///     learner_id UUID NOT NULL,\n///     badge_id   UUID NOT NULL,\n///     awarded_at TIMESTAMP WITH TIME ZONE NOT NULL,\n///     reason     TEXT NOT NULL,\n///     PRIMARY KEY (learner_id, badge_id)\n/// );\n/// ```\npub struct PgBadgeRepository {\n    pool: PgPool,\n}\n\nimpl PgBadgeRepository {\n    pub fn new(pool: PgPool) -> Self {\n        Self { pool }\n    }\n}\n\n#[async_trait]\nimpl BadgeRepository for PgBadgeRepository {\n    async fn learner_already_has_badge(\n        &self,\n        learner_id: Uuid,\n        badge_id: Uuid,\n    ) -> Result<bool, ServiceError> {\n        let res = sqlx::query_scalar!(\n            r#\"\n            SELECT EXISTS (\n                SELECT 1\n                FROM learner_badges\n                WHERE learner_id = $1 AND badge_id = $2\n            ) AS \"exists!\"\n            \"#,\n            learner_id,\n            badge_id\n        )\n        .fetch_one(&self.pool)\n        .await?;\n\n        Ok(res.unwrap_or(false))\n    }\n\n    async fn assign_badge(\n        &self,\n        learner_id: Uuid,\n        badge: &BadgeAwarded,\n    ) -> Result<(), ServiceError> {\n        sqlx::query!(\n            r#\"\n            INSERT INTO learner_badges (learner_id, badge_id, awarded_at, reason)\n            VALUES ($1, $2, $3, $4)\n            \"#,\n            learner_id,\n            badge.badge_id,\n            badge.awarded_at,\n            badge.reason\n        )\n        .execute(&self.pool)\n        .await?;\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n/// Business logic deciding whether a quiz submission qualifies\n/// for a badge.  Runs fully asynchronously, keeping its own\n/// subscription to the dispatcher.\n///\n/// Scoring rules used here are intentionally simple:  \n/// \u2013 Score \u2265 90 %      \u21d2 \u201cQuiz Master\u201d badge (UUID hard-coded)  \n/// \u2013 Score exactly 100 \u21d2 special \u201cPerfect Score\u201d badge\npub struct BadgeAwardService<R: BadgeRepository + 'static> {\n    repo: Arc<R>,\n    dispatcher: Dispatcher,\n    event_store: Arc<EventStore>,\n    subscribed_badges: HashSet<Uuid>,\n}\n\nimpl<R: BadgeRepository + 'static> BadgeAwardService<R> {\n    pub fn new(\n        repo: Arc<R>,\n        dispatcher: Dispatcher,\n        event_store: Arc<EventStore>,\n    ) -> Self {\n        // Hard-coded UUIDs of known badges.\n        let subscribed_badges = vec![\n            // \u201cQuiz Master\u201d\n            Uuid::parse_str(\"11111111-1111-1111-1111-111111111111\").unwrap(),\n            // \u201cPerfect Score\u201d\n            Uuid::parse_str(\"22222222-2222-2222-2222-222222222222\").unwrap(),\n        ]\n        .into_iter()\n        .collect();\n\n        Self {\n            repo,\n            dispatcher,\n            event_store,\n            subscribed_badges,\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Spawn the service on the Tokio runtime; returns its `JoinHandle`\n    /// so callers can `.await` graceful shutdown.\n    pub fn spawn(self: Arc<Self>) -> JoinHandle<()> {\n        let mut rx = self.dispatcher.subscribe();\n\n        tokio::spawn(async move {\n            loop {\n                select! {\n                    biased;\n\n                    // React to new events\n                    msg = rx.recv() => match msg {\n                        Ok(env) => {\n                            if let Err(e) = self.process_event(env).await {\n                                tracing::error!(\"BadgeAwardService failed: {e}\");\n                            }\n                        },\n                        Err(broadcast::error::RecvError::Closed) => {\n                            tracing::warn!(\"Dispatcher closed, BadgeAwardService exiting.\");\n                            break;\n                        },\n                        Err(broadcast::error::RecvError::Lagged(skipped)) => {\n                            tracing::warn!(\"BadgeAwardService lagged, skipped {skipped} messages\");\n                        },\n                    },\n\n                    // Allow cooperative cancellation.\n                    _ = tokio::time::sleep(Duration::from_secs(60)) => {},\n                }\n            }\n        })\n    }\n\n    async fn process_event(&self, env: EventEnvelope) -> Result<(), ServiceError> {\n        match env.event {\n            DomainEvent::QuizSubmitted(sub) => self.maybe_award_badge(sub).await?,\n            _ => { /* ignore */ }\n        }\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    async fn maybe_award_badge(&self, sub: QuizSubmitted) -> Result<(), ServiceError> {\n        // Determine qualifying badge.\n        let (badge_id, reason) = if (sub.score - 100.0).abs() < f32::EPSILON {\n            (\n                Uuid::parse_str(\"22222222-2222-2222-2222-222222222222\").unwrap(),\n                \"Perfect quiz score!\".to_owned(),\n            )\n        } else if sub.score >= 90.0 {\n            (\n                Uuid::parse_str(\"11111111-1111-1111-1111-111111111111\").unwrap(),\n                \"Scored 90% or above on a quiz.\".to_owned(),\n            )\n        } else {\n            return Ok(()); // Not eligible\n        };\n\n        // Filter unknown badge IDs (forward-compat).\n        if !self.subscribed_badges.contains(&badge_id) {\n            return Ok(());\n        }\n\n        // Idempotency check: learner may resubmit quiz multiple times.\n        if self\n            .repo\n            .learner_already_has_badge(sub.learner_id, badge_id)\n            .await?\n        {\n            return Ok(());\n        }\n\n        // Compose and persist badge award.\n        let badge = BadgeAwarded {\n            badge_id,\n            learner_id: sub.learner_id,\n            awarded_at: Utc::now(),\n            reason,\n        };\n\n        self.repo.assign_badge(sub.learner_id, &badge).await?;\n\n        let envelope = EventEnvelope::new(DomainEvent::BadgeAwarded(badge.clone()));\n        self.event_store.append(&envelope).await?;\n        self.dispatcher.publish(envelope).await;\n\n        tracing::info!(\n            learner=%sub.learner_id,\n            badge=%badge.badge_id,\n            \"Badge awarded!\"\n        );\n\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n// This module exposes:\n//!   * DomainEvent & DomainEventKind \u2013 strongly-typed, versioned event\n//!     definitions shared across bounded contexts.\n//!   * EventPublisher \u2013 service-layer abstraction allowing the core API to\n//!     remain ignorant of transport details (NATS, Kafka, etc.).\n//!   * NatsEventPublisher \u2013 production implementation that publishes JSON\n//!     envelopes to a NATS JetStream subject hierarchy.\n//!   * EventStore \u2013 ACID append-only persistence used for audit trail / GDPR\n//!     erase workflow.\n//!   * PostgresEventStore \u2013 repository implementation via `sqlx`.\n//!   * LearningPulseService \u2013 sample use-case that persists a new learning\n//!     pulse and emits the corresponding event within a single transaction.\n//!\n//! The code follows Repository + Service-Layer patterns and is intended to be\n//! wired up by the dependency-injection crate of your choice (e.g. `shuttle`,\n//! `axum::extract::State`, or `tower` layers).\n//!\n//! # Crate features required\n//! Make sure `Cargo.toml` enables the following dependencies:\n//!\n//! ```toml\n//! [dependencies]\n//! async-nats = { version = \"0.34\", default-features = false, features = [\"jetstream\"] }\n//! async-trait = \"0.1\"\n//! anyhow = \"1\"\n//! chrono = { version = \"0.4\", features = [\"serde\"] }\n//! serde = { version = \"1.0\", features = [\"derive\"] }\n//! serde_json = \"1.0\"\n//! sqlx = { version = \"0.7\", default-features = false, features = [\"runtime-tokio-rustls\", \"postgres\", \"chrono\", \"uuid\", \"json\"] }\n//! tokio = { version = \"1\", features = [\"macros\", \"rt-multi-thread\"] }\n//! tracing = \"0.1\"\n//! uuid = { version = \"1\", features = [\"serde\", \"v4\"] }\n//! ```\n//!\n//! ## Warning\n//! Production environments should tune JetStream options (e.g., stream\n//! retention), connection retries, and TLS settings. This sample is simplified\n//! for readability.\n\nuse std::sync::Arc;\n\nuse anyhow::{Context, Result};\nuse async_nats::jetstream::{self, stream::Stream};\nuse async_trait::async_trait;\nuse chrono::{DateTime, Utc};\nuse serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};\nuse sqlx::{postgres::PgQueryResult, PgPool, Postgres, Transaction};\nuse tracing::{debug, error, info, instrument};\nuse uuid::Uuid;\n\n// -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n// Domain Event Definitions\n// -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n/// Enum representing all event payloads produced by the **web_social** bounded\n/// context. Each variant must remain strictly additive (append-only) to avoid\n/// breaking consumers performing pattern matching.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\n#[serde(tag = \"type\", content = \"data\")]\n#[non_exhaustive]\npub enum DomainEventKind {\n    LessonPublished {\n        lesson_id: Uuid,\n        teacher_id: Uuid,\n    },\n    QuizSubmitted {\n        quiz_id: Uuid,\n        student_id: Uuid,\n        score_percentage: f32,\n    },\n    BadgeAwarded {\n        badge_id: Uuid,\n        student_id: Uuid,\n    },\n    PaymentProcessed {\n        payment_id: Uuid,\n        order_total_cents: i64,\n        payer_id: Uuid,\n    },\n    LearningPulseCreated {\n        pulse_id: Uuid,\n        teacher_id: Uuid,\n    },\n    LearningPulseResponded {\n        pulse_id: Uuid,\n        student_id: Uuid,\n        response_id: Uuid,\n    },\n}\n\n/// Envelope that wraps every event with rich metadata required for correlation\n/// and causation analysis.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct DomainEvent {\n    /// Unique ID for this event. Uses UUID v4 for randomness and horizontal\n    /// partitioning friendliness.\n    pub id: Uuid,\n    /// ID that allows grouping of events that belong to the same workflow.\n    pub correlation_id: Option<Uuid>,\n    /// ID of the event that directly triggered this one, if any.\n    pub causation_id: Option<Uuid>,\n    /// Actor responsible (user, system) \u2013 useful for audit trail.\n    pub actor_id: Option<Uuid>,\n    /// Time of creation in UTC with millisecond precision.\n    pub occurred_at: DateTime<Utc>,\n    /// Semantic version of the payload schema.\n    pub schema_version: u16,\n    /// Actual business payload.\n    pub payload: DomainEventKind,\n}\n\nimpl DomainEvent {\n    /// Creates a new envelope, stamping with `Utc::now()`.\n    pub fn new(actor_id: Option<Uuid>, payload: DomainEventKind) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            id: Uuid::new_v4(),\n            correlation_id: None,\n            causation_id: None,\n            actor_id,\n            occurred_at: Utc::now(),\n            schema_version: 1,\n            payload,\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Returns the recommended NATS subject where this event should be\n    /// published, following the `edupulse.{bounded_context}.{event_name}` style\n    /// to facilitate fine-grained subscriptions.\n    pub fn subject(&self) -> String {\n        let event_name = match &self.payload {\n            DomainEventKind::LessonPublished { .. } => \"lesson_published\",\n            DomainEventKind::QuizSubmitted { .. } => \"quiz_submitted\",\n            DomainEventKind::BadgeAwarded { .. } => \"badge_awarded\",\n            DomainEventKind::PaymentProcessed { .. } => \"payment_processed\",\n            DomainEventKind::LearningPulseCreated { .. } => \"learning_pulse_created\",\n            DomainEventKind::LearningPulseResponded { .. } => \"learning_pulse_responded\",\n        };\n        format!(\"edupulse.web_social.{}\", event_name)\n    }\n}\n\n// -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n// EventPublisher Abstraction\n// -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n/// Transport-agnostic publisher for domain events. Implementations must be\n/// idempotent and **MUST NOT** panic; failures are returned as `Err`.\n#[async_trait]\npub trait EventPublisher: Send + Sync {\n    async fn publish(&self, event: &DomainEvent) -> Result<()>;\n}\n\n// -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n// NATS JetStream Implementation\n// -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n/// Production-grade NATS JetStream publisher, supporting at-least-once delivery.\n/// Uses JSON serialisation for maximum interoperability with polyglot services.\npub struct NatsEventPublisher {\n    client: async_nats::Client,\n    jetstream: jetstream::Context,\n    stream: Stream,\n}\n\nimpl NatsEventPublisher {\n    /// Creates a new publisher, auto-provisioning the `edupulse` stream if it\n    /// does not exist. The stream is configured for message-size budgets\n    /// typical to domain events (< 64 KiB).\n    pub async fn new(nats_url: &str) -> Result<Self> {\n        let client = async_nats::connect(nats_url).await?;\n        let jetstream = jetstream::new(client.clone());\n\n        let stream = match jetstream.get_stream(\"EDUPULSE\").await {\n            Ok(stream) => stream,\n            Err(_) => {\n                info!(\"creating JetStream stream `EDUPULSE`\");\n                jetstream\n                    .create_stream(jetstream::stream::Config {\n                        name: \"EDUPULSE\".to_owned(),\n                        subjects: vec![\"edupulse.>\".to_owned()],\n                        max_age: chrono::Duration::days(7).to_std().unwrap(),\n                        storage: jetstream::stream::StorageType::File,\n                        ..Default::default()\n                    })\n                    .await?\n            }\n        };\n\n        Ok(Self {\n            client,\n            jetstream,\n            stream,\n        })\n    }\n}\n\n#[async_trait]\nimpl EventPublisher for NatsEventPublisher {\n    #[instrument(skip_all, fields(event_id = %event.id, subject = %event.subject()))]\n    async fn publish(&self, event: &DomainEvent) -> Result<()> {\n        let bytes = serde_json::to_vec(event)?;\n        self.client\n            .publish(event.subject(), bytes.into())\n            .await\n            .context(\"failed to publish event to NATS\")?;\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n// -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n// Event Store Repository\n// -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n/// Append-only store for domain events, enabling event sourcing and audit trail\n/// reconstruction. .await?;\n\n        rows.into_iter()\n            .map(|row| {\n                let value: serde_json::Value = row.payload;\n                let ev: DomainEvent = serde_json::from_value(value)\n .context(\"failed to insert learning pulse\")?;\n\n        debug!(rows_affected = q.rows_affected(), \"inserted learning pulse\");\n\n        // Build domain event.\n        let event = DomainEvent::new(\n            Some(dto.teacher_id),\n            DomainEventKind::LearningPulseCreated {\n                pulse_id,\n                teacher_id: dto.teacher_id,\n            },\n We log the error and continue \u2013 state is\n            // durable because the event is stored.\n            error!(error = %e, \"failed to publish learning_pulse_created\");\n        }\n\n        Ok(LearningPulse {\n            id: pulse_id,\n            teacher_id: dto.teacher_id,\n            title: dto.title,\n            description: dto.description,\n            due_date: dto.due_date,\n            created_at: Utc::now(),\n        })\n    }\n}\n\n// -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n// SQL bootstrap helpers (optional)\n// -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n/// Executes the  required DDL statements if they do not yet exist. Event-driven infrastructure for **EduPulse Live \u2013 Event-Driven Social Learning\n//! Hub**.  This module materialises the *Domain Event* concept mentioned in the\n//! architecture description and provides a pluggable, async publisher that can\n//! be wired to a real message-broker (e.g. RabbitMQ via *lapin*) or gracefully\n//! degrade to a pure in-process logger in tests or local development.\n//!\n//! Key design points\n//! -----------------\n//! \u2022 A strongly-typed `DomainEvent` enum prevents the *stringly-typed* antipattern.  \n//! \u2022 An `EventEnvelope` carries universal metadata used by downstream services.  \n//! \u2022 The `EventPublisher` trait abstracts the transport; a concrete\n//!   `RabbitMqPublisher` is behind a crate feature flag (`broker`).  \n//! \u2022 `thiserror` provides ergonomic error handling.  \n//! \u2022 `async_trait` allows `async` functions in traits while staying on stable Rust.\n//!\n//! -----------------------------------------------------------------------------\n//! Crate features\n//! --------------\n//! `broker` \u2013 Enables the real AMQP publisher that talks to RabbitMQ.  When the\n//! feature is **not** enabled, a lightweight logger implementation is compiled\n//! instead. This keeps test binaries small and fast.\n//!\n//! -----------------------------------------------------------------------------\n//! External crates\n//! ---------------\n//!  - `serde`, `serde_json`  \u2013 (de)serialisation\n//!  - `uuid`                \u2013 event correlation / id\n//!  - `chrono`              \u2013 timestamps with timezone\n//!  - `async_trait`         \u2013 async in traits\n//!  - `thiserror`           \u2013 error enums\n//!  - `log`                 \u2013 structured logging facade\n//!  - `lapin`               \u2013 AMQP client  (only with `broker` feature)\n//!  - `tokio`               \u2013 async runtime, required by lapin\n//! -----------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n#![allow(clippy::large_enum_variant)]\n\nuse std::time::Duration;\n\nuse async_trait::async_trait;\nuse chrono::{DateTime, Utc};\nuse serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};\nuse thiserror::Error;\nuse uuid::Uuid;\n\n#[cfg(feature = \"broker\")]\nuse {\n    lapin::{\n        options::BasicPublishOptions,\n        publisher_confirm::Confirmation,\n        types::FieldTable,\n        BasicProperties, Channel, Connection, ConnectionProperties,\n    },\n    tokio::time::timeout,\n};\n\n/// Maximum time we wait for the broker to confirm our message.\n///\n/// The constant is visible because tests may want to shorten the interval with\n/// `tokio::time::pause`.\npub const PUBLISH_CONFIRM_TIMEOUT: Duration = Duration::from_secs(3);\n\n/// Common metadata added to **every** event before leaving the bounded context.\n///\n/// The data is intentionally generic and keeps the envelope small so that\n/// high-volume events remain cheap to serialize and ship.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct EventMetadata {\n    /// Globally unique identifier used for idempotence and correlation.\n    pub id: Uuid,\n\n    /// RFC3339 timestamp indicating when the event was created at the source.\n    pub occurred_at: DateTime<Utc>,\n\n    /// Name of the bounded context / micro-service that originally emitted this\n    /// event (e.g. `eduplse.api`, `eduplse.analytics-svc`).\n    pub source: String,\n\n    /// Optional correlation id (e.g. HTTP request id) allowing us to trace the\n    /// causal chain across service boundaries.\n    #[serde(skip_serializing_if = \"Option::is_none\")]\n    pub correlation_id: Option<Uuid>,\n}\n\nimpl Default for EventMetadata {\n    fn default() -> Self {\n        Self {\n            id: Uuid::new_v4(),\n            occurred_at: Utc::now(),\n            source: env!(\"CARGO_PKG_NAME\").to_owned(),\n            correlation_id: None,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// The **DomainEvent** enum encapsulates the canonical vocabulary for the\n/// EduPulse domain.  Each variant is versioned so we can evolve payloads\n/// without breaking existing subscribers.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\n#[serde(tag = \"type\", content = \"payload\")]\npub enum DomainEvent {\n    /// A teacher has published a new lesson.\n    LessonPublishedV1 {\n        lesson_id: Uuid,\n        title: String,\n        author_id: Uuid,\n    },\n\n    /// A student submitted answers to a quiz.\n    QuizSubmittedV1 {\n        quiz_id: Uuid,\n        attempt_id: Uuid,\n        student_id: Uuid,\n    },\n\n    /// A peer gave feedback to someone else's submission.\n    PeerFeedbackGivenV1 {\n        feedback_id: Uuid,\n        submission_id: Uuid,\n        reviewer_id: Uuid,\n    },\n\n    /// A student was granted a badge.\n    BadgeAwardedV1 {\n        badge_id: Uuid,\n        awardee_id: Uuid,\n        reason: String,\n    },\n\n    /// Money changed hands for a premium micro-course.\n    PaymentCapturedV1 {\n        payment_id: Uuid,\n        amount_cents: i64,\n        currency: String,\n        payer_id: Uuid,\n    },\n}\n\n/// Envelope that wraps the event payload with universal metadata.\n///\n/// Storing metadata *outside* the payload makes it trivial to evolve individual\n/// events without duplicating the same bookkeeping fields everywhere.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct EventEnvelope {\n    pub meta: EventMetadata,\n    pub event: DomainEvent,\n}\n\nimpl EventEnvelope {\n    pub fn new<E: Into<DomainEvent>>(event: E) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            meta: EventMetadata::default(),\n            event: event.into(),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Serialise the envelope into a compact JSON payload.\n///\n/// We purposefully avoid pretty printing for network efficiency; producers that\n/// want human-readable output can call `pretty_json()` instead.\nimpl EventEnvelope {\n    pub fn to_json_bytes(&self) -> Result<Vec<u8>, EventError> {\n        Ok(serde_json::to_vec(self)?)\n    }\n\n    #[allow(dead_code)]\n    pub fn pretty_json(&self) -> Result<String, EventError> {\n        Ok(serde_json::to_string_pretty(self)?)\n    }\n\n    /// Derive the *logical* routing key used in AMQP brokers.  Topic exchange\n    /// policies can fan-out events to multiple queues, e.g. `lesson.published.v1`.\n    pub fn routing_key(&self) -> String {\n        match &self.event {\n            DomainEvent::LessonPublishedV1 { .. } => \"lesson.published.v1\",\n            DomainEvent::QuizSubmittedV1 { .. } => \"quiz.submitted.v1\",\n            DomainEvent::PeerFeedbackGivenV1 { .. } => \"feedback.given.v1\",\n            DomainEvent::BadgeAwardedV1 { .. } => \"badge.awarded.v1\",\n            DomainEvent::PaymentCapturedV1 { .. } => \"payment.captured.v1\",\n        }\n        .into()\n    }\n}\n\n/// Error type for publishing and serialisation failures.\n#[derive(Error, Debug)]\npub enum EventError {\n    #[error(\"serialization error: {0}\")]\n    Serialization(#[from] serde_json::Error),\n\n    #[cfg(feature = \"broker\")]\n    #[error(\"amqp error: {0}\")]\n    Amqp(#[from] lapin::Error),\n\n    #[error(\"broker confirmation timed out\")]\n    ConfirmationTimeout,\n\n    #[error(\"other: {0}\")]\n    Other(String),\n}\n\n/// Trait every publisher (mock or real) must implement.\n///\n/// The abstraction enables dependency injection in application services and\n/// makes *unit* testing simpler:  we can just inject the `LoggingPublisher`.\n#[async_trait]\npub trait EventPublisher: Send + Sync {\n    async fn publish(&self, envelope: EventEnvelope) -> Result<(), EventError>;\n}\n\n/// A publisher that merely writes events to the `log` sink.\n///\n/// Enabled by default, also used when the `broker` feature is disabled. The\n/// design means the rest of the application can always depend on\n/// `dyn EventPublisher`, regardless of compilation mode.\npub struct LoggingPublisher;\n\n#[async_trait]\nimpl EventPublisher for LoggingPublisher {\n    async fn publish(&self, envelope: EventEnvelope) -> Result<(), EventError> {\n        // Format into single-line JSON to keep log ingestion systems happy.\n        let json = envelope.to_json_bytes()?;\n        // Safe because JSON is UTF-8.\n        log::info!(\n            target: \"eduplse.events\",\n            \"event={} meta_id={} payload={}\",\n            envelope.routing_key(),\n            envelope.meta.id,\n            String::from_utf8_lossy(&json)\n        );\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n/// Real AMQP publisher that talks to RabbitMQ.  \n///\n/// Compiled **only** when the `broker` feature is present.  Uses publisher\n/// confirms so we know the broker durably persisted the message.\n#[cfg(feature = \"broker\")]\npub struct RabbitMqPublisher {\n    channel: Channel,\n    exchange: String,\n}\n\n#[cfg(feature = \"broker\")]\nimpl RabbitMqPublisher {\n    /// Connect to the AMQP broker and prepare the channel.\n    ///\n    /// A production-grade implementation would configure TLS, heartbeat, and\n    /// automatic reconnection. Those details are omitted for brevity.\n    pub async fn connect(\n        amqp_uri: &str,\n        exchange: &str,\n    ) -> Result<Self, EventError> {\n        let connection = Connection::connect(\n            amqp_uri,\n            ConnectionProperties::default().with_default_executor(8),\n        )\n        .await\n        .map_err(EventError::from)?;\n\n        let channel = connection.create_channel().await?;\n        channel\n            .confirm_select(lapin::options::ConfirmSelectOptions::default())\n            .await?;\n\n        Ok(Self {\n            channel,\n            exchange: exchange.to_owned(),\n        })\n    }\n}\n\n#[cfg(feature = \"broker\")]\n#[async_trait]\nimpl EventPublisher for RabbitMqPublisher {\n    async fn publish(&self, envelope: EventEnvelope) -> Result<(), EventError> {\n        let payload = envelope.to_json_bytes()?;\n        let routing_key = envelope.routing_key();\n\n        let confirm: Confirmation = self\n            .channel\n            .basic_publish(\n                &self.exchange,\n                &routing_key,\n                BasicPublishOptions {\n                    mandatory: false,\n                    immediate: false,\n                },\n                &payload,\n                BasicProperties::default().with_content_type(\"application/json\"),\n            )\n            .await?\n            .await?; // Wait for broker confirm (publisher confirms must be enabled)\n\n        // lapin returns Nack(\u2026) in error path; we check for `Ack`.\n        if !confirm.is_ack() {\n            return Err(EventError::Other(format!(\n                \"broker did not acknowledge event id {}\",\n                envelope.meta.id\n            )));\n        }\n\n        // Additionally enforce a timeout because `await?` can hang if broker is\n        // misconfigured (e.g., confirm_select was forgotten).\n        timeout(PUBLISH_CONFIRM_TIMEOUT, async {\n            while !confirm.is_ack() {}\n        })\n        .await\n        .map_err(|_| EventError::ConfirmationTimeout)?;\n\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n/// When compiled **without** the `broker` feature, alias [`LoggingPublisher`]\n/// to `DefaultPublisher` to satisfy DI containers effortlessly.\n///\n/// ```\n/// use eduplse::events::DefaultPublisher;\n/// let publisher = DefaultPublisher;\n/// ```\n#[cfg(not(feature = \"broker\"))]\npub type DefaultPublisher = LoggingPublisher;\n\n#[cfg(feature = \"broker\")]\npub type DefaultPublisher = RabbitMqPublisher;\n\n//\n// Performer\".into(),\n        });\n\n        let json = ev.to_json_bytes().unwrap();\n        let deser: EventEnvelope = serde_json::from_slice(&json).unwrap();\n\n        assert_eq!(ev.meta.id, deser.meta.id);\n        match deser.event {\n            DomainEvent::BadgeAwardedV1 { reason, .. } => {\n                assert_eq!(reason, \"Top Performer\");\n            }\n            _ => = LoggingPublisher;\n            let env = EventEnvelope::new(DomainEvent::LessonPublishedV1 {\n                lesson_id: Uuid::new_v4(),\n                title: \"Async in Rust\".into(),\n Dependencies (Cargo.toml excerpt):\n//! ----------------------------------\n//! async-nats = { version = \"0.33\", default-features = false, features = [\"tls\"] }\n//! sqlx       = { version = \"0.7\", features = [\"runtime-tokio-native-tls\", \"postgres\", \"json\"] }\n//! serde      = { version = \"1.0\", features = [\"derive\"] }\n//! serde_json = \"1.0\"\n//! thiserror  = \"1.0\"\n//! uuid       = { version = \"1.3\", features = [\"v4\", \"serde\"] }\n//! chrono     = { version = \"0.4\", features = [\"serde\"] }\n//! tracing    = \"0.1\"\n//! futures    = \"0.3\"\n//! anyhow     = \"1.0\"\n//! ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\nuse std::sync::Arc;\n\nuse async_nats::{Client as NatsClient, PublishAck};\nuse chrono::{DateTime, Utc};\nuse futures::{Stream, StreamExt, TryStreamExt};\nuse serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};\nuse sqlx::{postgres::PgPoolOptions, PgPool, Postgres, Transaction};\nuse thiserror::Error;\nuse tracing::{instrument, span, Level};\nuse uuid::Uuid;\n\n/// Type alias for the *canonical* aggregate identifier.\n/// (We keep it generic enough to be shared among all contexts.)\npub type AggregateId = Uuid;\n\n/// A type-safe identifier used for exactly-once message guarantees.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, Hash, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct EventId(Uuid);\n\nimpl Default for EventId {\n    fn default() -> Self {\n        EventId(Uuid::new_v4())\n    }\n}\n\n/// Core domain events.\n///\n/// NOTE: In a real system this enum would live in its own crate and be shared\n/// through the workspace. default.\npub type Result<T, E = EventError> = std::result::Result<T, E>;\n\n/// Data-access abstraction for the event store.\n///\n/// Implementation uses *optimistic concurrency control* (OCC) via a `seq`\n/// column coupled with a *partial unique index* on (`aggregate_id`, `seq`).\n#[derive(Clone)]\npub struct EventStore {\n    pool: Arc<PgPool>,\n}\n\nimpl EventStore {\n    pub async fn connect(database_url: &str, max_connections: u32) -> Result<Self> {\n        let pool = PgPoolOptions::new()\n            .max_connections(max_connections)\n            .after_connect(|mut conn, _meta| {\n                Box::pin(async move {\n                    // Force UTC timezone for timestamp determinism.\n                    sqlx::query(\"SET TIME ZONE 'UTC'\").execute(&mut conn).await?;\n                    Ok(())\n                })\n            })\n            .connect(database_url)\n            .await?;\n\n        Ok(Self {\n            pool: Arc::new(pool),\n        })\n    }\n\n    /// Append a *single* event to the store with OCC.\n    ///\n    /// Returns the stored [`EventEnvelope`] (with auto-generated id + timestamp).\n    #[instrument(skip(self, tx))]\n    pub async fn append_one(\n        &self,\n        mut tx: Transaction<'_, Postgres>,\n        aggregate_id: AggregateId,\n        expected_seq: i64,\n        event: DomainEvent,\n        correlation_id: Option<EventId>,\n    ) -> Result<EventEnvelope> {\n        // Next sequence number we intend to store.\n        let next_seq = expected_seq + 1;\n\n        let envelope = EventEnvelope::new(aggregate_id, next_seq, event, correlation_id);\n        let serialized = serde_json::to_value(&envelope)?;\n\n        let res = sqlx::query(\n            r#\"\n            INSERT INTO event_store (id, aggregate_id, seq, payload)\n            VALUES ($1, $2, $3, $4)\n            ON CONFLICT (aggregate_id, seq) DO NOTHING\n            \"#,\n        )\n        .bind(envelope.id.0)\n        .bind(envelope.aggregate_id)\n        .bind(envelope.seq)\n        .bind(&serialized)\n        .execute(&mut *tx)\n        .await?;\n\n        if res.rows_affected() == 0 {\n            // Sequence already taken \u2013 someone else wrote concurrently.\n            let actual = self\n                .latest_sequence_for(&aggregate_id)\n                .await?\n                .unwrap_or_default();\n\n            return Err(EventError::Concurrency {\n                aggregate_id,\n                expected: expected_seq,\n                actual,\n            });\n        }\n\n        Ok(envelope)\n    }\n\n    /// Returns the *last* known sequence for an aggregate.  If absent, returns\n    /// `None`.\n    #[instrument(skip(self))]\n    pub async fn latest_sequence_for(&self, aggregate_id: &AggregateId) -> Result<Option<i64>> {\n        let seq = sqlx::query_scalar::<_, Option<i64>>(\n            r#\"\n            SELECT seq\n            FROM event_store\n            WHERE aggregate_id = $1\n            ORDER BY seq DESC\n            LIMIT 1\n            \"#,\n        )\n        .bind(aggregate_id)\n        .fetch_one(&*self.pool)\n        .await?;\n\n        Ok(seq)\n    }\n\n    /// Open an *unbounded* stream for the whole event log.\n    /// Clients should apply their own back-pressure strategies.\n    #[instrument(skip(self))]\n    pub fn stream_all(&self) -> impl Stream<Item = Result<EventEnvelope>> + '_ {\n        sqlx::query_scalar::<_, serde_json::Value>(\n            r#\"SELECT payload FROM event_store ORDER BY id\"#,\n        )\n        .fetch(&*self.pool)\n        .map_ok(|val| serde_json::from_value::<EventEnvelope>(val))\n        .try_buffered(64) // concurrent JSON deserialization\n    }\n\n    /// Helper to begin a transaction.\n    pub async fn begin(&self) -> Result<Transaction<'_, Postgres>> {\n        Ok(self.pool.begin().await?)\n    }\n}\n\n/// Publishes events to NATS with at-least-once semantics.\n///\n/// It is intentionally *thin*: we keep transport concerns outside domain\n/// services.\n#[derive(Clone)]\npub struct EventPublisher {\n    nats: NatsClient,\n    subject_prefix: Arc<str>,\n}\n\nimpl EventPublisher {\n    pub async fn connect(nats_url: &str, subject_prefix: impl AsRef<str>) -> Result<Self> {\n        // TLS enabled by default (async_nats w/ `tls` feature).\n        let nats = async_nats::connect(nats_url).await?;\n\n        Ok(Self {\n            nats,\n            subject_prefix: Arc::from(subject_prefix.as_ref()),\n        })\n    }\n\n    fn subject_for(&self, event: &DomainEvent) -> String {\n        // Use enum variant name as the subject suffix.\n        let variant = match event {\n            DomainEvent::LessonPublished { .. } => \"LessonPublished\",\n            DomainEvent::QuizSubmitted { .. } => \"QuizSubmitted\",\n            DomainEvent::BadgeAwarded { .. } => \"BadgeAwarded\",\n            DomainEvent::PaymentProcessed { .. } => \"PaymentProcessed\",\n        };\n        format!(\"{}.{}\", self.subject_prefix, variant)\n    }\n\n    /// Publish an envelope to NATS.  Returns the `PublishAck`.\n    #[instrument(skip(self, envelope))]\n    pub async fn publish(&self, envelope: &EventEnvelope) -> Result<PublishAck> {\n        let subject = self.subject_for(&envelope.event);\n        let payload = serde_json::to_vec(envelope)?;\n\n        Ok(self.nats.publish(subject, payload.into()).await?)\n    }\n}\n\n/// High-level facade combining the store and broker for transactional\n/// *outbox*-style consistency.\n///\n/// Usage:\n///\n/// ```rust,no_run\n/// let ctx = EventContext::new(store, publisher);\n/// ctx.commit(|tx| async move {\n///     // ... domain logic mutating aggregates ...\n///     ctx.append(tx, aggregate_id, expected_seq, event).await?;\n///     Ok(())\n/// }).await?;\n/// ```\n#[derive(Clone)]\npub struct EventContext {\n    store: EventStore,\n    publisher: EventPublisher,\n}\n\nimpl EventContext {\n    pub fn new(store: EventStore, publisher: EventPublisher) -> Self {\n        Self { store, publisher }\n    }\n\n    /// Wrap a *business* operation in a transaction and publish all newly\n    /// appended events atomically (two-phase commit).\n    #[instrument(skip(self, op))]\n    pub async fn commit<F, Fut, T>(&self, op: F) -> Result<T>\n    where\n        F: FnOnce(&Self, &mut Transaction<'_, Postgres>) -> Fut + Send + Sync,\n        Fut: std::future::Future<Output = Result<T>> + Send,\n        T: Send,\n    {\n        let mut tx = self.store.begin().await?;\n\n        let result = op(self, &mut tx).await?;\n\n        // Extract fresh events written within the tx:\n        let staged_events: Vec<EventEnvelope> = sqlx::query_scalar(\n            r#\"\n            SELECT payload\n            FROM event_store\n            WHERE transaction_timestamp() - statement_timestamp() < INTERVAL '1 second'\n              AND txid_current() = txid_current()\n            \"#,\n        )\n        .fetch_all(&mut *tx)\n        .await?\n        .into_iter()\n        .map(|val: serde_json::Value| serde_json::from_value(val))\n        .collect::<std::result::Result<_, _>>()?;\n\n        // Commit DB first (outbox pattern).\n        tx.commit().await?;\n\n        // Publish *after* commit to avoid phantom events.\n        for env in staged_events {\n            // We could `spawn` but prefer sequential to simplify ordering/acks.\n            self.publisher.publish(&env).await?;\n        }\n\n        Ok(result)\n    }\n\n    /// Convenience wrapper: append + publish inside a running tx.\n    #[instrument(skip(self, tx))]\n    pub async fn append(\n        &self,\n        tx: &mut Transaction<'_, Postgres>,\n        aggregate_id: AggregateId,\n        expected_seq: i64,\n        event: DomainEvent,\n        correlation_id: Option<EventId>,\n    ) -> Result<EventEnvelope> {\n        let env = self\n            .store\n            .append_one(\n                tx.as_mut(),\n                aggregate_id,\n                expected_seq,\n                event,\n                correlation_id,\n            )\n            .await?;\n\n        // Buffer the event in the transaction\u2019s local temp table for later pickup.\n        sqlx::query(\n            r#\"\n            INSERT INTO _staged_events (payload) VALUES ($1)\n            \"#,\n        )\n        .bind(sqlx::types::Json(&env))\n        .execute(&mut *tx)\n        .await?;\n\n        Ok(env)\n    }\n}\n\n// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n// Database bootstrap helpers (run via migrations)\n// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n/// Creates the *event_store* table and helper structures.\n///\n/// Called by the migration runner (e.g., refinery, sqlx-migrate).\npub async fn bootstrap_event_schema(pool: &PgPool) -> anyhow::Result<()> {\n    let mut conn = pool.acquire().await?;\n\n    // Use idempotent `IF NOT EXISTS` to keep it re-runnable.\n    sqlx::query(\n        r#\"\n        CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS event_store (\n            id            UUID            PRIMARY KEY,\n            aggregate_id  UUID            NOT NULL,\n            seq           BIGINT          NOT NULL,\n            payload       JSONB           NOT NULL,\n\n            CONSTRAINT seq_unique UNIQUE (aggregate_id, seq)\n        );\n\n        -- Fast lookup for aggregates\n        CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_event_store_aggregate\n            ON event_store (aggregate_id);\n\n        -- Staging area for outbox pattern (tx-scoped)\n ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n// Tests (can run w/ `cargo test -- --ignored` once a local PG + NATS exists)\n// must be set for integration tests\");\n        let nats_url = env::var(\"NATS_URL\").unwrap_or_else(|_| \"tls://localhost:4222\".into());\n\n        let store = EventStore::connect(&db, 5).await?;\n        bootstrap_event_schema(&store.pool).await?;\n\n        let publisher = EventPublisher::connect(&nats_url, \"edupulse.events\").await?;\n        let ctx = EventContext::new(store.clone(),
