This module wires domain events to asynchronous handlers while persisting\n//! them into an append-only event store.  Designed to live inside the core API\n//! crate, it exposes a minimal fa\u00e7ade so that higher-level modules\n//! (lessons/quizzes/auth/etc.) can remain agnostic of the underlying message\n//! transport.\n//!\n//! Highlights\n//! ----------\n//! \u2022 Tokio-powered, back-pressure-aware broadcast channel  \n//! \u2022 Pluggable `EventStore` (in-memory + SQLx/Postgres ref. impl)  \n//! \u2022 Dynamic subscription registry using `async_trait` + `DashMap`  \n//! \u2022 JSON-serialised events for wire compatibility (RabbitMQ/NATS/etc.)  \n//! \u2022 Tracing-instrumented for observability\n//!\n//! Usage\n//! -----\n//! ```rust,no_run\n//! let event_bus = Arc::new(EventBus::new(InMemoryEventStore::default()));\n//! event_bus.start_worker_pool(4);                    // spawn background workers\n//! event_bus.register_handler(SearchIndexer::new()?); // Tantivy search handler\n//! event_bus.emit(DomainEvent::LessonPublished {...}).await?;\n//! ```\n\nuse std::{\n    sync::Arc,\n    time::{SystemTime, UNIX_EPOCH},\n};\n\nuse anyhow::{Context, Result};\nuse async_trait::async_trait;\nuse dashmap::DashMap;\nuse serde::{de::DeserializeOwned, Deserialize, Serialize};\nuse tokio::{\n    select,\n    spawn,\n    sync::{broadcast, mpsc},\n    task::JoinHandle,\n};\nuse tracing::{debug, error, info, instrument, warn};\nuse uuid::Uuid;\n\n/// Default broadcast channel capacity (per Tokio docs, power of two for perf)\nconst CHANNEL_CAPACITY: usize = 1 << 8;\n\n/// All domain-level events that flow through the platform.\n///\n/// When this enum grows large, consider splitting variants into separate enums\n/// and boxing them in an `enum`/`trait object` for compile-time boundary\n/// management.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\n#[serde(tag = \"type\", content = \"data\")]\npub enum DomainEvent {\n    LessonPublished {\n        lesson_id: Uuid,\n        author_id: Uuid,\n        title: String,\n        published_at: UnixTimestamp,\n    },\n    QuizSubmitted {\n        quiz_id: Uuid,\n        student_id: Uuid,\n        score: u8,\n        submitted_at: UnixTimestamp,\n    },\n    // --- truncated: add more events as needed ---\n}\n\n/// Simple millisecond-precision unix timestamp wrapper.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, PartialOrd, Ord, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct UnixTimestamp(u64);\n\nimpl Default for UnixTimestamp {\n    fn default() -> Self {\n        Self(\n            SystemTime::now()\n                .duration_since(UNIX_EPOCH)\n                .expect(\"time went backwards\")\n                .as_millis() as u64,\n        )\n    }\n}\n\n/// Persistence fa\u00e7ade for storing domain events.\n///\n/// The event store is append-only and can be replayed for audits, projections\n/// or rebuilding read models.\n#[async_trait]\npub trait EventStore: Send + Sync + 'static {\n    async fn append(&self, event: &DomainEvent) -> Result<()>;\n    async fn stream_all<E>(&self) -> Result<Vec<E>>\n    where\n        E: DeserializeOwned + Send + 'static;\n}\n\n/// In-memory reference implementation; suitable for tests / dev playground.\n#[derive(Debug, Default)]\npub struct InMemoryEventStore {\n    events: tokio::sync::RwLock<Vec<Vec<u8>>>,\n}\n\n#[async_trait]\nimpl EventStore for InMemoryEventStore {\n    #[instrument(skip(self, event))]\n    async fn append(&self, event: &DomainEvent) -> Result<()> {\n        let payload = serde_json::to_vec(event).context(\"serialising event\")?;\n        self.events.write().await.push(payload);\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    async fn stream_all<E>(&self) -> Result<Vec<E>>\n    where\n        E: DeserializeOwned + Send + 'static,\n    {\n        let raw = self.events.read().await.clone();\n        let mut out = Vec::with_capacity(raw.len());\n        for bytes in raw {\n            let evt = serde_json::from_slice::<E>(&bytes).context(\"deserialising\")?;\n            out.push(evt);\n        }\n        Ok(out)\n    }\n}\n\n/// Event handler contract.\n///\n/// Note: we purposefully consume by value (`self`) to allow stateful handlers to\n/// move into the async task when registered.\n#[async_trait]\npub trait EventHandler: Send + Sync + 'static {\n    /// A human-readable name for observability.\n    fn name(&self) -> &'static str;\n\n    /// Business logic invoked for each event.\n    async fn handle(&self, evt: DomainEvent) -> Result<()>;\n}\n\n/// Thread-safe, async event bus.\n#[derive(Debug)]\npub struct EventBus<S: EventStore> {\n    tx: broadcast::Sender<DomainEvent>,\n    store: Arc<S>,\n    handlers: DashMap<&'static str, Box<dyn EventHandler>>,\n    /// Workers receive events from the broadcast channel and sequentially\n    /// deliver them to handlers (de-duplicated per handler).\n    worker_txs: Vec<mpsc::Sender<DomainEvent>>,\n}\n\nimpl<S: EventStore> EventBus<S> {\n    pub fn new(store: S) -> Self {\n        let (tx, _rx) = broadcast::channel(CHANNEL_CAPACITY);\n        Self {\n            tx,\n            store: Arc::new(store),\n            handlers: DashMap::new(),\n            worker_txs: Vec::new(),\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Emit a single event.\n    #[instrument(skip(self))]\n    pub async fn emit(&self, evt: DomainEvent) -> Result<()> {\n        self.store.append(&evt).await?;\n        self.tx\n            .send(evt)\n            .map_err(|e| anyhow::anyhow!(\"broadcast failure: {e}\"))?;\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    /// Register a handler; idempotent per handler name.\n    pub fn register_handler<H>(&self, handler: H)\n    where\n        H: EventHandler,\n    {\n        if self.handlers.insert(handler.name(), Box::new(handler)).is_some() {\n            warn!(\"handler {} replaced at runtime\", handler.name());\n        } else {\n            info!(\"handler {} registered\", handler.name());\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Spawn a worker pool that fans-out events to handlers.\n    ///\n    /// Each worker owns an mpsc channel (to avoid contention) and reads from\n    /// the *same* broadcast channel.  This guarantees at-least-once delivery to\n    /// each handler.\n    pub fn start_worker_pool(self: &Arc<Self>, workers: usize) -> Vec<JoinHandle<()>> {\n        let mut handles = Vec::with_capacity(workers);\n        for id in 0..workers {\n            let (tx, mut rx) = mpsc::channel::<DomainEvent>(CHANNEL_CAPACITY);\n            self.worker_txs.push(tx);\n\n            let bus = Arc::clone(self);\n            let mut broadcast_rx = bus.tx.subscribe();\n            handles.push(spawn(async move {\n                info!(worker = id, \"event worker started\");\n                loop {\n                    select! {\n                        Ok(evt) = broadcast_rx.recv() => {\n                            // fan-in to single queue\n                            if let Err(e) = rx.try_send(evt) {\n                                debug!(%e, worker = id, \"worker queue full; dropping\");\n                            }\n                        },\n\n                        Some(evt) = rx.recv() => {\n                            for item in bus.handlers.iter() {\n                                let handler = item.value();\n                                let evt_clone = evt.clone();\n                                let h_name = handler.name();\n                                let res = handler.handle(evt_clone).await;\n                                if let Err(e) = res {\n                                    error!(%e, handler = h_name, \"event handler failed\");\n                                }\n                            }\n                        }\n                    }\n                }\n            }));\n        }\n        handles\n    }\n}\n\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n/* ----------------------- Example Production Handler ----------------------- */\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n\n/// Tantivy-powered search indexer.\n///\n/// In a real deployment this would:\n/// 1. Open a persistent `Index` directory;\n/// 2. Map domain events to documents;\n/// 3. Commit in batches for throughput.\npub struct SearchIndexer {\n    // index: tantivy::Index,\n}\n\nimpl SearchIndexer {\n    pub fn new() -> Result<Self> {\n        // let index = tantivy::Index::open_or_create(...)?;\n        Ok(Self {\n            // index,\n        })\n    }\n}\n\n#[async_trait]\nimpl EventHandler for SearchIndexer {\n    fn name(&self) -> &'static str {\n        \"search_indexer\"\n    }\n\n    #[instrument(skip(self))]\n    async fn handle(&self, evt: DomainEvent) -> Result<()> {\n        match evt {\n            DomainEvent::LessonPublished {\n                lesson_id,\n                title,\n                author_id,\n                ..\n            } => {\n                debug!(\n                    ?lesson_id,\n                    %title,\n                    ?author_id,\n                    \"indexing lesson into search engine\"\n                );\n                // let mut writer = self.index.writer(50_000_000)?;\n                // writer.add_document(...);\n                // writer.commit()?;\n            }\n            _ => { /* ignore other events */ }\n        }\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n/* ------------------------------- Unit Tests ------------------------------- */\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n    use std::time::Duration;\n\n    #[tokio::test(flavor = \"multi_thread\", worker_threads = 2)]\n    async fn event_roundtrip() -> Result<()> {\n        tracing_subscriber::fmt::try_init().ok();\n\n        let bus = Arc::new(EventBus::new(InMemoryEventStore::default()));\n        bus.register_handler(SearchIndexer::new()?);\n        bus.start_worker_pool(2);\n\n        let evt = DomainEvent::LessonPublished {\n            lesson_id: Uuid::new_v4(),\n            author_id: Uuid::new_v4(),\n            title: \"Rust for Edu-preneurs\".into(),\n            published_at: UnixTimestamp::default(),\n        };\n        bus.emit(evt.clone()).await?;\n\n        // allow some processing time\n        tokio::time::sleep(Duration::from_millis(250)).await;\n\n        // ensure event persisted\n        let events: Vec<DomainEvent> = bus.store.stream_all().await?;\n        assert_eq!(events.len(), 1);\n        assert!(matches!(events[0], DomainEvent::LessonPublished { .. }));\n\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n```",

This module encapsulates everything required to reliably publish domain\n//! events to an external broker while guaranteeing atomic persistence of the\n//! associated business transaction (Transactional Outbox pattern).\n//!\n//! A high-level overview of the workflow:\n//!\n//! 1.  Business service saves its state changes inside a SQL transaction.\n//! 2.  The same transaction stores an `OutboxEvent` row\n//!     inside `event_outbox` (JSONB payload).\n//! 3. tokio::time::sleep;\nuse tracing::{debug, error, info, instrument};\n\n/// The global NATS subject for EduPulse Live domain events.\n///\n/// Each microservice subscribes using its own durable Deserialize)]\npub struct EventEnvelope<E: DomainEvent> {\n    pub event_id: uuid::Uuid,\n    pub event_type: &'static str,\n    pub version: &'static str,\n    pub occurred_at: DateTime<Utc>,\n    pub aggregate_id: uuid::Uuid,\n    pub payload: E,\n}\n\n/// Helper to wrap a concrete event instance.\npub fn wrap_event<E: DomainEvent>(\n    aggregate_id: uuid::Uuid,\n    payload: E,\n) -> EventEnvelope<E> {\n    EventEnvelope {\n        event_id: uuid::Uuid::new_v4(),\n        event_type: payload.event_type(),\n        version: payload.version(),\n        occurred_at: Utc::now(),\n table.\n///\n/// Must be invoked within the caller's SQL transaction.\n#[instrument(skip(tx, envelope))]\npub async fn persist_event<E>(\n    tx: &mut Transaction<'_, Postgres>,\n    envelope: &EventEnvelope<E>,\n) -> Result<(), OutboxError>\nwhere\n    E: DomainEvent,\n{\n    let payload_json = serde_json::to_value(&envelope.payload)?;\n    sqlx::query!(\n        r#\"\n        INSERT INTO ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n/// Number of events we fetch per batch to reduce DB contention.\nconst BATCH_SIZE: i64 = {0}\")]\n    Serde(#[from] serde_json::Error),\n\n    #[error(\"NATS error: {0}\")]\n    Nats(#[from] async_nats::Error),\n}\n\n/// Background worker which iteratively drains the `event_outbox` table\n/// and forwards the events to NATS JetStream.\npub struct OutboxProcessor {\n    pg_pool: PgPool,\n    nats: jetstream::Context,\n}\n\nimpl OutboxProcessor {\n    /// Constructs a new [`OutboxProcessor`].\n    pub async fn new(pg_pool: PgPool, nats_url: &str) -> Result<Self, OutboxError> {\n        let nats_client = NatsClient::connect_with_options(\n            nats_url,\n            ConnectOptions::with_name(\"edupulse-outbox\"),\n        )\n        .await?;\n        let jetstream = jetstream::new(nats_client);\n\n        Ok(Self {\n            pg_pool,\n            nats: jetstream,\n        })\n    }\n\n    /// Starts the infinite polling loop until `shutdown` future resolves.\n    ///\n    /// Caller decides the sleep interval between attempts.\n    #[instrument(skip(self, shutdown), name = \"outbox.run\")]\n    pub async fn run_until_stopped(\n        &self,\n        poll_interval: Duration,\n        mut shutdown: tokio::sync::watch::Receiver<()>,\n    ) {\n        loop {\n            tokio::select! {\n                _ = shutdown.changed() => {\n                    info!(\"Outbox processor received shutdown signal \u2013 finishing current batch\");\n                    break;\n                }\n                _ = self.tick() => {}\n            }\n\n            sleep(poll_interval).await;\n        }\n\n        info!(\"Outbox processor terminated gracefully\");\n    }\n\n    /// Execute a single polling cycle.\n    #[instrument(skip(self))]\n    pub async fn tick(&self) {\n        match self.process_batch().await {\n            Ok(count) => {\n                if count > 0 {\n                    info!(count, \"outbox events dispatched\");\n                } else {\n                    debug!(\"no events to dispatch\");\n                }\n            }\n            Err(err) => {\n                error!(?err, \"failed to process outbox batch\");\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Fetch a batch of pending events, publish, and mark as dispatched.\n    #[instrument(skip(self), err)]\n    async fn process_batch(&self) -> Result<u64, OutboxError> {\n        let mut tx = self.pg_pool.begin().await?;\n\n        // Step 1: select for update \u2013 prevents concurrent processors\n        let events: Vec<OutboxEvent> = sqlx::query_as!(\n            OutboxEvent,\n            r#\"\n            SELECT * FROM event_outbox\n            WHERE published_at IS NULL\n            ORDER BY id\n            FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED\n            LIMIT $1\n            \"#,\n            BATCH_SIZE\n        )\n        .fetch_all(&mut tx)\n        .await?;\n\n        if events.is_empty() {\n            tx.rollback().await?;\n            return Ok(0);\n        }\n\n        // Step 2: publish each event to NATS\n        for evt in &events {\n            let payload_bytes = serde_json::to_vec(&evt)?;\n            self.nats\n                .publish(NATS_SUBJECT, payload_bytes.into())\n                .await?;\n        }\n\n        // Step 3: update published stamp\n        sqlx::query!(\n            r#\"\n            UPDATE event_outbox\n            SET published_at = NOW()\n            WHERE id = ANY($1)\n            \"#,\n            &events.iter().map(|e| e.id).collect::<Vec<_>>()\n        )\n        .execute(&mut tx)\n        .await?;\n\n        tx.commit().await?;\n        Ok(events.len() as u64)\n    }\n}\n\n/// ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n/// Example domain event\n/// Deserialize)]\npub struct LearningPulseCreated {\n    pub pulse_id: uuid::Uuid,\n    pub author_id: uuid::Uuid,\n    pub title: String,\n    pub summary: String,\n}\n\nimpl DomainEvent for LearningPulseCreated {\n    fn event_type(&self) -> &'static str {\n        \"learning_pulse.created\"\n    }\n\n    fn version(&self) -> &'static str {\n        \"1.0\"\n    }\n}\n\n/// ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n/// Convenience API for application services\n/// ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n/// Publish a newly generated domain event inside an existing SQL transaction.\n///\n/// Typical usage in a service command handler:\n///\n/// ```ignore\n/// let mut tx = pool.begin().await?;\n/// let envelope = wrap_event(aggregate_id, LearningPulseCreated { \u2026 });\n/// persist_event(&mut tx, &envelope).await?;\n/// tx.commit().await?;\n/// ```\npub async fn publish_domain_event<E>(\n    tx: &mut Transaction<'_, Postgres>,\n    aggregate_id: uuid::Uuid,\n    event: E,\n) -> Result<(), OutboxError>\nwhere\n    E: DomainEvent,\n{\n    let envelope = wrap_event(aggregate_id, event);\n    persist_event(tx, &envelope).await\n}\n```",

Defining domain-event primitives used across bounded contexts.\n//  2.  Persisting events to Postgres (append-only event store).\n//  3.  Publishing events to NATS for inter-service communication.\n//\n//  The implementation follows the Repository + Service Layer pattern.\n//  All operations are asynchronous and cancellation-safe.\n//\n//  Production quality considerations:\n//\n//  \u2022   Events are idempotent (id is always generated server-side).\n//  \u2022   Structured logging via `tracing`.\n//  \u2022   Resilient error handling with `thiserror`.\n//  \u2022   Secure JSON serialization (deny unknown fields).\n//  \u2022   Observability hooks (OpenTelemetry compatible).\n//\n//  To keep the example self-contained, migrations and consumer side are\n//  omitted. In a real deployment, refer to `migrations/20240229101000_create_event_store.sql`.\n\n#![allow(clippy::missing_docs_in_private_items)]\n\nuse std::time::Duration;\n\nuse async_nats::{Client as NatsClient, ConnectionOptions};\nuse async_trait::async_trait;\nuse chrono::{DateTime, Utc};\nuse serde::{de::DeserializeOwned, Deserialize, Serialize};\nuse sqlx::{postgres::PgPoolOptions, PgPool, }\n}\n\n/// ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n/// EVENT STORE (POSTGRES) + PUBLISHER (NATS)\n/// publication.\n#[derive(Clone)]\npub struct EventBus {\n    db: PgPool,\n    nats: NatsClient,\n}\n\nimpl EventBus {\n    /// Establish a new [`EventBus`] from environment variables:\n    ///   DATABASE_URL, NATS_URL, NATS_TOKEN (optional).\n    pub async fn from_env() -> Result<Self, EventBusError> {\n        let database_url = std::env::var(\"DATABASE_URL\")\n            .map_err(|_| EventBusError::MissingEnvVar(\"DATABASE_URL\".into()))?;\n        let nats_url =\n            std::env::var(\"NATS_URL\").unwrap_or_else(|_| \"nats://127.0.0.1:4222\".to_string());\n\n        let db = })\n    }\n\n    ///   Persist + publish a single domain event.\n    ///\n    ///   Atomicity guarantees:\n    ///   1. Publish\n        self.publish_to_bus(&envelope).await?;\n\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    /// Append event to the Postgres event store.\n    async fn append_to_store<T>(&self, envelope: .push_bind(envelope.aggregate_id)\n                    .push_bind(T::kind())\n                    .push_bind(envelope.occurred_at)\n                    .push_bind(payload_json);\n            },\n T::kind();\n\n        timeout(\n            IO_TIMEOUT,\n            self.nats\n                .publish(subject.into(), payload.into())\n                .await\n                .map(|_| ()),\n        )\n        .await\n        .map_err(|_| EventBusError::Timeout)?\n        .map_err(EventBusError::MessageBroker)?;\n\n        info!(subject, \"Event published to NATS\");\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n self.repo.fetch_unsent(self.max_batch).await?;\n\n            if events.is_empty() {\n                sleep(self.poll_every).await;\n                continue;\n            }\n\n            // We use a .map(|evt| {\n                    let conn = &nats_conn;\n                    async move {\n                        conn.publish(evt.subject(), serde_json::to_vec(&evt)?)\n                            .await\n                            .map_err(OutboxError::from)\n                    }\n                })\n                .buffer_unordered(16)\n                .collect::<Vec<_>>();\n\n results.into_iter().partition(Result::is_ok);\n\n            if !oks.is_empty() {\n                // Only mark events sent when the publish actually succeeded.\n                let sent_events: Vec<_> = events\n                    .iter()\n                    .zip(oks)\n                    .filter_map(|(evt, res)| res.ok().map(|_| evt.clone()))\n                    .collect();\n\n                self.repo.mark_sent(&sent_events).await?;\n            }\n\n            if !errs.is_empty() {\n                // Log and backoff; caller decides global error handling.\n                tracing::warn!(\n                    failed = errs.len(),\n                    \"Some messages failed to publish; will retry\"\n                );\n                // Exponential-ish backoff for noisy neighbours.\n                sleep(self.poll_every * 2).await;\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    fn sign_payload(&self, envelope: &EventEnvelope) -> Result<String, OutboxError> {\n        let mut bytes = serde_json::to_vec(envelope)\n            .map_err(|e| OutboxError::Other(format!(\"serde: {e}\")))?;\n\n        // Sign the raw bytes (comment this if you prefer canonical JSON).\n        let sig = self.key_pair.sign(&mut bytes);\n        Ok(base64::encode(sig.as_ref()))\n    }\n}\n\n/// Example domain event.\n///\n/// In real code these live inside domain modules; kept here for This module provides a production-ready* implementation of the\n//! Outbox/Inbox pattern for EduPulse Live.  All domain events are first\n//! persisted inside the same Postgres transaction that modified the\n//! aggregate and are later *atomically* published to the message broker\n//! (e.g. RabbitMQ).  This guarantees *at-least-once* delivery without\n//! sacrificing database consistency.\n//!\n//! # Architecture\n//! 1. Domain layer inserts a row into the `outbox_events` table\n//!    through [`OutboxRepository::insert`].\n//! 2. [`OutboxProcessor`] polls the table on an interval (or is triggered\n//!    by NOTIFY/LISTEN) and publishes unpublished events.\n//! 3. After a successful publish it marks the event as `published_at`.\n//!\n//! # Usage\n//! ```no_run\n//! #[tokio::main]\n//! async fn main() -> anyhow::Result<()> {\n//!     env_logger::init();\n//!\n//!     let db = PgPoolOptions::new()\n//!         .max_connections(5)\n//!         .connect(\"postgres://user:password@localhost/edupulse\")\n//!         .await?;\n//!\n//!     // Initialise AMQP connection\n//!     let amqp_addr = \"amqp://guest:guest@127.0.0.1:5672/%2f\";\n//!     let publisher = RabbitMqPublisher::connect(amqp_addr, \"edupulse.events\").await?;\n//!\n//!     // Fire-and-forget background processing task\n//!     OutboxProcessor::spawn(db.clone(), publisher);\n//!\n//!     // \u2026 start REST API, etc.\n//!     Ok(())\n//! }\n//! ```\n//! *Error handling, retries, and back-off have been implemented but can be\n//! expanded with metrics, dead-letter queues, etc.*\n\nuse std::sync::Arc;\nuse std::time::Duration;\n\nuse async_trait::async_trait;\nuse backoff::{future::retry, ExponentialBackoff};\nuse chrono::{DateTime, Utc};\nuse lapin::{\n    options::{BasicPublishOptions, QueueDeclareOptions},\n    types::FieldTable,\n    BasicProperties, Channel, Connection, ConnectionProperties,\n};\nuse log::{error, info, warn};\nuse serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};\nuse sqlx::{postgres::PgRow, PgPool, Row};\nuse thiserror::Error;\nuse tokio::{\n    sync::Mutex,\n    task::{self, JoinHandle},\n    time,\n};\nuse uuid::Uuid;\n\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n/*                                Domain Event                                */\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n\n/// A single row inside the `outbox_events` table.\n///\n/// NOTE: `payload` is stored as **raw JSON** to keep the table generic and\n/// future-proof.  Consumers can decode it based on the `event_type`.\n#[derive(Debug, Serialize, Deserialize, Clone)]\npub struct OutboxEvent {\n    pub id: Uuid,\n    pub aggregate_type: String,\n    pub aggregate_id: Uuid,\n    pub event_type: String,\n    pub payload: serde_json::Value,\n    pub occurred_at: DateTime<Utc>,\n    pub published_at: Option<DateTime<Utc>>,\n}\n\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n/*                                  Errors                                    */\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n\n#[derive(Error, Debug)]\npub enum OutboxError {\n    #[error(\"database error: {0}\")]\n    Database(#[from] sqlx::Error),\n\n    #[error(\"AMQP error: {0}\")]\n    Amqp(#[from] lapin::Error),\n\n    #[error(\"serialization error: {0}\")]\n    Serde(#[from] serde_json::Error),\n}\n\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n/*                           Outbox Repository (DAO)                          */\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n\n/// Repository responsible for accessing the `outbox_events` table.\n#[derive(Clone)]\npub struct OutboxRepository {\n    pool: PgPool,\n}\n\nimpl OutboxRepository {\n    pub fn new(pool: PgPool) -> Self {\n        Self { pool }\n    }\n\n    /// Inserts a new [`OutboxEvent`] within an existing transaction or\n    /// standalone if `tx` is `None`.\n    pub async fn insert(\n        &self,\n        mut event: OutboxEvent,\n        tx: Option<&mut sqlx::Transaction<'_, sqlx::Postgres>>,\n    ) -> Result<OutboxEvent, OutboxError> {\n        event.id = event.id; // ensure id exists\n        let query = sqlx::query!(\n            r#\"\n            INSERT INTO outbox_events (\n                id,\n                aggregate_type,\n                aggregate_id,\n                event_type,\n                payload,\n                occurred_at,\n                published_at\n            ) VALUES ($1,$2,$3,$4,$5,$6,$7)\n            \"#,\n            event.id,\n            event.aggregate_type,\n            event.aggregate_id,\n            event.event_type,\n            event.payload,\n            event.occurred_at,\n            event.published_at\n        );\n\n        match tx {\n            Some(tx_ref) => {\n                query.execute(&mut *tx_ref).await?;\n            }\n            None => {\n                query.execute(&self.pool).await?;\n            }\n        }\n\n        Ok(event)\n    }\n\n    /// Fetches a batch of unpublished events, ordered by `occurred_at`.\n    pub async fn fetch_unpublished(\n        &self,\n        limit: i64,\n    ) -> Result<Vec<OutboxEvent>, OutboxError> {\n        let rows = sqlx::query(\n            r#\"\n            SELECT\n                id,\n                aggregate_type,\n                aggregate_id,\n                event_type,\n                payload,\n                occurred_at,\n                published_at\n            FROM outbox_events\n            WHERE published_at IS NULL\n            ORDER BY occurred_at\n            LIMIT $1\n            \"#,\n        )\n        .bind(limit)\n        .map(|row: PgRow| OutboxEvent {\n            id: row.get(\"id\"),\n            aggregate_type: row.get(\"aggregate_type\"),\n            aggregate_id: row.get(\"aggregate_id\"),\n            event_type: row.get(\"event_type\"),\n            payload: row.get::<serde_json::Value, _>(\"payload\"),\n            occurred_at: row.get(\"occurred_at\"),\n            published_at: row.get(\"published_at\"),\n        })\n        .fetch_all(&self.pool)\n        .await?;\n\n        Ok(rows)\n    }\n\n    /// Marks the event as published.\n    pub async fn mark_as_published(&self, id: Uuid) -> Result<(), OutboxError> {\n        sqlx::query!(\n            r#\"\n            UPDATE outbox_events\n            SET published_at = NOW()\n            WHERE id = $1\n            \"#,\n            id\n        )\n        .execute(&self.pool)\n        .await?;\n\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n/*                             Event Publisher                                */\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n\n/// Trait that abstracts away the underlying message broker implementation.\n/// This allows swapping RabbitMQ for NATS, Kafka, etc. without touching the\n/// domain/application layer.\n#[async_trait]\npub trait EventPublisher: Send + Sync + 'static {\n    async fn publish(&self, event: &OutboxEvent) -> Result<(), OutboxError>;\n}\n\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n/*                             RabbitMQ Publisher                             */\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n\n/// Thin wrapper around a RabbitMQ channel that implements [`EventPublisher`].\n#[derive(Clone)]\npub struct RabbitMqPublisher {\n    channel: Arc<Channel>,\n    exchange: String,\n}\n\nimpl RabbitMqPublisher {\n    /// Establishes a connection and ensures that the declared exchange exists.\n    pub async fn connect(\n        amqp_addr: &str,\n        exchange: &str,\n    ) -> Result<Self, OutboxError> {\n        let conn = Connection::connect(amqp_addr, ConnectionProperties::default()).await?;\n        let channel = conn.create_channel().await?;\n\n        channel\n            .queue_declare(\n                exchange,\n                QueueDeclareOptions::default(),\n                FieldTable::default(),\n            )\n            .await?;\n\n        Ok(Self {\n            channel: Arc::new(channel),\n            exchange: exchange.to_string(),\n        })\n    }\n}\n\n#[async_trait]\nimpl EventPublisher for RabbitMqPublisher {\n    async fn publish(&self, event: &OutboxEvent) -> Result<(), OutboxError> {\n        let payload = serde_json::to_vec(event)?;\n        self.channel\n            .basic_publish(\n                \"\",\n                &self.exchange,\n                BasicPublishOptions::default(),\n                &payload,\n                BasicProperties::default()\n                    .with_content_type(\"application/json\".into())\n                    .with_message_id(event.id.to_string().into())\n                    .with_type(event.event_type.clone().into()),\n            )\n            .await?\n            .await?; // wait for broker confirmation\n\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n/*                            Outbox Processor                                */\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n\n/// Responsible for periodically polling the DB, publishing events and\n/// updating their status. It runs indefinitely in a tokio task.\npub struct OutboxProcessor {\n    handle: JoinHandle<()>,\n}\n\nimpl OutboxProcessor {\n    /// Spawns the background `OutboxProcessor` task with sensible defaults.\n    ///\n    /// `poll_interval` defaults to 500 ms and `batch_size` to 100.\n    pub fn spawn<P>(pool: PgPool, publisher: P) -> Self\n    where\n        P: EventPublisher,\n    {\n        let poll_interval = Duration::from_millis(500);\n        let batch_size = 100;\n\n        let repo = OutboxRepository::new(pool);\n        let publisher = Arc::new(publisher);\n\n        let handle = task::spawn(async move {\n            let mut interval = time::interval(poll_interval);\n            loop {\n                interval.tick().await;\n                if let Err(err) =\n                    Self::drain_batch(&repo, Arc::clone(&publisher), batch_size).await\n                {\n                    error!(\"Error draining outbox: {:?}\", err);\n                }\n            }\n        });\n\n        Self { handle }\n    }\n\n    async fn drain_batch<P>(\n        repo: &OutboxRepository,\n        publisher: Arc<P>,\n        batch_size: i64,\n    ) -> Result<(), OutboxError>\n    where\n        P: EventPublisher,\n    {\n        // Fetch a batch; early return if empty\n        let events = repo.fetch_unpublished(batch_size).await?;\n        if events.is_empty() {\n            return Ok(());\n        }\n\n        // Publish events sequentially (could be parallel with `join_all` if\n        // ordering isn't important)\n        for event in events {\n            let op = || async {\n                publisher.publish(&event).await?;\n                repo.mark_as_published(event.id).await?;\n                Ok::<(), OutboxError>(())\n            };\n\n            // Retry with exponential back-off (max ~10 min)\n            let mut backoff = ExponentialBackoff {\n                initial_interval: Duration::from_millis(250),\n                multiplier: 2.0,\n                max_interval: Duration::from_secs(30),\n                max_elapsed_time: Some(Duration::from_secs(600)),\n                ..Default::default()\n            };\n\n            if let Err(err) = retry(backoff, op).await {\n                // This should rarely happen; send to Sentry, Dead-letter, etc.\n                warn!(\"Failed to publish event {}: {:?}\", event.id, err);\n            }\n        }\n\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    /// Waits for the background task to finish (e.g. on graceful shutdown).\n    pub async fn join(self) -> Result<(), task::JoinError> {\n        self.handle.await\n    }\n}\n\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n/*                                   Tests                                    */\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n    use sqlx::Executor;\n    use tokio::sync::Mutex;\n\n    /// Dummy EventPublisher for MockPublisher {\n        async fn publish(&self, _event: &OutboxEvent) -> Result<(), OutboxError> {\n            let mut guard = self.published.lock().await;\n            *guard += 1;\n            Ok(())\n        }\n    }\n\n    #[sqlx::test(migrations = \"../migrations\")]\n    async fn processor_publishes_and_marks_event(pool: PgPool) -> Result<(), Box<dyn std::error::Error>>\n    {\n        // Arrange\n        let repo = OutboxRepository::new(pool.clone());\n        let publisher = MockPublisher::default();\n        let now = Utc::now();\n\n        let event = OutboxEvent {\n            id: Uuid::new_v4(),\n            aggregate_type: \"Lesson\".into(),\n            aggregate_id: Uuid::new_v4(),\n            event_type: \"LessonPublished\".into(),\n            payload: serde_json::json!({\"title\": \"Intro\"}),\n            occurred_at: now,\n            published_at: None,\n        };\n\n        repo.insert(event.clone(), None).await?;\n\n        // Act\n        OutboxProcessor::drain_batch(&repo, Arc::new(publisher.clone()), 10).await?;\n\n        // Assert\n        let unpublished = repo.fetch_unpublished(10).await?;\n        assert!(unpublished.is_empty(), \"event should be marked as published\");\n\n        let hits = *publisher.published.lock().await;\n        assert_eq!(hits, 1, \"event should have been published exactly once\");\n\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n```",

The module follows a classical Service/Repository split and is completely\n//! unit-testable thanks to its fully mockable trait interfaces.\n//!\n//! # Examples\n//! ```no_run\n//! use edupulse_live::pulse::service::{PulseService, ServiceConfig};\n//! use edupulse_live::pulse::repository::InMemoryPulseRepository;\n//! use edupulse_live::infra::broker::NatsPublisher;\n//! use std::sync::Arc;\n//! use uuid::Uuid;\n//!\n//! #[tokio::main]\n//! async fn main() -> anyhow::Result<()> {\n//!     let repo = Arc::new(InMemoryPulseRepository::default());\n//!     let publisher = Arc::new(NatsPublisher::connect(\"nats://localhost:4222\").await?);\n//!\n//!     let svc = PulseService::new(ServiceConfig::default(), repo, publisher);\n//!\n//!     let teacher_id = Uuid::new_v4();\n//!     let pulse_id = svc\n//!         .create_pulse(teacher_id, \"Explain async/await in Rust\".into())\n//!         .await?;\n//!\n//!     let student_id = Uuid::new_v4();\n//!     svc.reply_to_pulse(pulse_id, student_id, \"Here is my explanation\u2026\".into())\n//!         .await?;\n//! RepositoryError> {\n        let guard = self.store.read();\n        Ok(guard.get(&id).cloned())\n    }\n\n    async fn upsert(&self, pulse: Pulse) -> Result<(), RepositoryError> {\n        let mut guard = self.store.write();\n        guard.insert(pulse.id, pulse);\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n/* ---------- Message Broker Abstraction ---------- */\n\n#[async_trait]\npub trait EventPublisher: Ok(Self {\n            nats_url,\n            creds,\n            prefix,\n            internal_buffer: 1024,\n        })\n    }\n}\n\n/// Tokio-aware streaming receiver produced by {\n                Ok(ev) => return Some(ev),\n                Err(broadcast::error::RecvError::Lagged(_)) => {\n                    error!(\"subscriber lagged behind event stream\");\n Wild-cards supported\n    /// (`*` for token, `>` for all remaining).\n    async fn subscribe(&self, subject: String) -> Result<EventStream, BusError>;\n\n    /// Gracefully close all connections / fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {\n        f.debug_struct(\"NatsEventBus\")\n            .field(\"cfg\", &self.cfg)\n            .finish()\n    }\n}\n\nimpl NatsEventBus {\n {e}\");\n                }\n            });\n        }\n\n        Ok(bus)\n    }\n\n    /// Long-running task that forwards NATS messages to [`broadcast::Sender`].\n    #[cfg(not(feature = \"in_memory_bus\"))]\n    async fn run_inbound_pump(self: Arc<Self>) -> Result<(), BusError> {\n        let subject = format!(\"{}.*\", self.cfg.prefix);\n        let mut sub = self.nats.subscribe(subject).await?;\n\n        loop {\n            select! {\n                msg = sub.next() => {\n                    match msg {\n                        Some(m) => self.forward_inbound(m).await?,\n                        None => break,\n                    }\n                }\n                // Add graceful shutdown signal here if needed\n            }\n EventBus for NatsEventBus {\n    #[instrument(skip(self, event))]\n    async fn publish(&self, event: DomainEvent) -> Result<(), BusError> {\n        let subject = format!(\"{}.{}\", self.cfg.prefix, event.event_type);\n        let payload = serde_json::to_vec(&event)?;\n        #[cfg(not(feature = \"in_memory_bus\"))]\n        self.nats.publish(subject, payload.into()).await?;\n }\n\n        let rx = self.tx.subscribe();\n        Ok(EventStream { rx })\n    }\n\n    async fn close(&self) -> Result<(), BusError> {\n        // Closing broadcast::Sender drops all receivers.\n The trait is intentionally narrow\n/// so that adapters for DynamoDB, Kafka-compacted topics, or filesystem\n/// snapshots can be added later with minimal friction.\n#[async_trait]\npub trait EventStore: Send + Sync {\n    async fn append_event(&self, event: &AuditEvent) -> Result<(), EventStoreError>;\n    async fn fetch_events_by_aggregate(\n        &self,\n        aggregate_id: Uuid,\n    ) -> Result<Vec<AuditEvent>, EventStoreError>;\n    /// GDPR-style erase. match pool {\n            Some(p) => Ok(Self { pool: p }),\n            None => {\n                let db_url = env::var(\"DATABASE_URL\")\n                    .map_err(|_|             let pool = PgPool::builder()\n                    .max_size(max_conns)\n                    .build(&db_url)\n                    .await?;\n                Ok(Self { pool })\n            }\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n#[async_trait]\nimpl EventStore for PgEventStore {\n    #[instrument(skip_all, fields(event_id=%event.event_id))]\n    async fn append_event(&self, event: &AuditEvent) -> $4, $5)\n            \"#,\n        )\n        .bind(event.event_id)\n        .bind(event.aggregate_id)\n        .bind(event.event_type.clone())\n        .bind(&event.payload)\n        .bind(event.created_at)\n        .execute(&self.pool)\n        .await?;\n\n        info!(%event.event_id, \"event persisted\");\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    #[instrument(skip_all, sqlx::query(\n            r#\"\n            SELECT event_id, aggregate_id, event_type, payload, created_at\n            FROM audit_events\n            WHERE aggregate_id = $1\n            ORDER BY created_at ASC\n            \"#,\n        )\n        .bind(aggregate_id)\n        .fetch_all(&self.pool)\n        .await?;\n\n        let events = rows.into_iter().map(row_to_event).collect::<Result<_, _>>()?;\n        Ok(events)\n    }\n\n    /// Iterates through *all* events where `aggregate_id = user_id`, then\n    /// transforms the JSON Runs inside a\n    /// `BEGIN \u2026 COMMIT` block to guarantee atomicity.\n    #[instrument(skip_all, fields(user_id=%user_id))]\n    async fn pseudonymise_user(\n        &self,\n        user_id: Uuid,\n        pseudonym: &str,\n    ) -> Result<(), EventStoreError> {\n        let mut tx = self.pool.begin().await?;\n\n        let affected: i64 = sqlx::query_scalar(\n            r#\"\n            SELECT COUNT(*) FROM audit_events\n            WHERE aggregate_id = $1\n            \"#,\n        )\n        .bind(user_id)\n        .fetch_one(&mut *tx)\n        .await?;\n\n        if affected == 0 {\n            return Err(EventStoreError::UnknownUser(user_id));\n        }\n\n        // Fetch, transform, write back\n        let rows = sqlx::query(\n            r#\"\n            SELECT event_id, aggregate_id, event_type, payload, created_at\n            FROM audit_events\n            WHERE aggregate_id = $1\n            \"#,\n        )\n        .bind(user_id)\n        .fetch_all(&mut *tx)\n        .await?;\n\n        for row in rows {\n            let mut event = row_to_event(row)?;\n            event.payload = pseudonymise_payload(&event.payload, pseudonym)?;\n            sqlx::query(\n                r#\"\n                UPDATE audit_events\n                SET payload = $1\n                WHERE event_id = $2\n                \"#,\n            )\n            .bind(&event.payload)\n            .bind(event.event_id)\n            .execute(&mut *tx)\n            .await?;\n        }\n\n        tx.commit().await?;\n        info!(%user_id, \"pseudonymisation complete ({} events)\", affected);\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n/// Convert a database row into `AuditEvent`.\nfn row_to_event(row: PgRow) -> Result<AuditEvent, EventStoreError> {\n    Ok(AuditEvent {\n        event_id: row.try_get(\"event_id\")?,\n        aggregate_id: row.try_get(\"aggregate_id\")?,\n        event_type: row.try_get(\"event_type\")?,\n        payload: row.try_get(\"payload\")?,\n        created_at: row.try_get(\"created_at\")?,\n    })\n}\n\n/// Recurse through JSON to strip direct identifiers (name, email, \u2026) and\n/// replace them with a constant pseudonym.  This is obviously simplistic,\n/// but demonstrates the technique.  Real-world code would leverage schema\n/// introspection or build explicit per-event transformers.\nfn pseudonymise_payload(\n    original: &JsonValue,\n    pseudonym: &str,\n) -> Result<JsonValue, EventStoreError> {\n    let mut clone = original.clone();\n\n    match &mut clone {\n        JsonValue::Object(map) => {\n            static SENSITIVE_KEYS: &[&str] = &[\"name\", \"email\", \"first_name\", \"last_name\"];\n            for key in SENSITIVE_KEYS {\n                if map.contains_key(*key) {\n                    map.insert((*key).to_string(), JsonValue::String(pseudonym.to_owned()));\n                }\n            }\n            // Recurse into nested values\n            for v in map.values_mut() {\n                *v = pseudonymise_payload(v, pseudonym)?;\n            }\n        }\n        JsonValue::Array(arr) => {\n            for v in arr.iter_mut() {\n                *v = pseudonymise_payload(v, pseudonym)?;\n            }\n        }\n        _ => { /* primitives stay unchanged */ }\n    }\n    Ok(clone)\n}\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n    use serde_json::json;\n\n    #[tokio::test]\n    async fn test_pseudonymise_payload() {\n        let original = json!({\n            \"name\": \"Alice\",\n            \"email\": \"alice@example.com\",\n            \"score\": 95,\n            \"nested\": {\n                \"first_name\": \"Alice\",\n                \"comments\": [\"great job\"]\n            }\n        });\n\n        let transformed = pseudonymise_payload(&original, \"redacted\").unwrap();\n        assert_eq!(transformed[\"name\"], \"redacted\");\n        assert_eq!(transformed[\"nested\"][\"first_name\"], \"redacted\");\n        assert_eq!(transformed[\"score\"], 95); // untouched\n    }\n\n    #[tokio::test]\n    async fn test_append_and_fetch_roundtrip() -> Result<(), Box<dyn std::error::Error>> {\n        // Spin up a transient in-memory Postgres in CI or use `TEST_DATABASE_URL`.\n        let db_url =\n            std::env::var(\"TEST_DATABASE_URL\").unwrap_or_else(|_| \"postgres://postgres@localhost/ep_test\".into());\n        let pool = PgPool::connect(&db_url).await?;\n        // Ensure table exists for the test\n        sqlx::query(\n            r#\"\n            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS audit_events (\n                event_id     UUID PRIMARY KEY,\n                aggregate_id UUID NOT NULL,\n                event_type   VARCHAR NOT NULL,\n                payload      JSONB NOT NULL,\n                created_at   TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL\n            );\n            \"#,\n        )\n        .execute(&pool)\n        .await?;\n\n        let store = PgEventStore::new(Some(pool.clone())).await?;\n\n        let event = AuditEvent {\n            event_id: Uuid::new_v4(),\n            aggregate_id: Uuid::new_v4(),\n            event_type: DomainEventType::LessonPublished,\n            payload: json!({\"lesson_id\": 42, \"title\": \"Rust Ownership\"}),\n            created_at: Utc::now(),\n        };\n\n        store.append_event(&event).await?;\n        let fetched = store.fetch_events_by_aggregate(event.aggregate_id).await?;\n        assert_eq!(fetched.len(), 1);\n        assert_eq!(fetched[0].payload[\"lesson_id\"], 42);\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n```",

Responsibilities\n//! ----------------\n//! \u25cf CRUD + domain validation for `LearningPulse` aggregate  \n//! \u25cf Emission of domain events that other bounded\u2013contexts subscribe to  \n//! \u25cf Infrastructure\u2010agnostic repository + pluggable event broker  \n//!\n//! The code is *production-grade* in that it\n//!   - hides infrastructure behind traits,\n//!   - surfaces rich error types,\n//!   - is fully async,\n//!   - embraces immutability and strong typing,\n//!   - contains exhaustive tests (see `#[cfg(test)]`).\n//!\n//! }\n}\n\n/// Public aggregate root.\n#[derive(Clone, Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct LearningPulse {\n    pub id: PulseId,\n    pub author_id: Uuid,\n    pub title: String,\n    pub       }\n\n        let pulse = LearningPulse {\n            id: PulseId::new(),\n            author_id,\n            title,\n            description,\n            created_at: Utc::now(),\n        };\n\n        let event = DomainEvent::PulseCreated(PulseCreated {\n            pulse_id: pulse.id,\n            author_id,\n            occurred_at: pulse.created_at,\n        });\n\n        Ok((pulse, event))\n    }\n}\n\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n/*                             Domain Event System                            */\n/*   "content": "# Solution: rust_web_social_expert_073_architectural_understanding_expert_01\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nThis architectural analysis examines the EduPulse Live platform, an event-driven social learning system built in Rust. The platform follows a CQRS (Command Query Responsibility Segregation) architecture with an event-sourcing pattern. After thorough analysis of the codebase, I have identified the core architectural components, traced a complete data flow, and developed a strategic integration plan for the proposed Real-time Collaborative Whiteboard feature.\n\n---\n\n## Key Files Identified\n\n### Configuration and Infrastructure\n- `/app/project/src/config.txt` - Application configuration with database, broker, auth, and search settings\n- `/app/project/package.json` - Frontend dependencies including socket.io-client for real-time communications\n\n### Authentication & Session Management\n- `/app/project/src/module_1.txt` - **AuthenticationService** - JWT-based authentication with Redis session management, bcrypt password hashing, and role-based access control\n\n### Event Bus Infrastructure\n- `/app/project/src/module_4.txt` - **EventPublisher & EventStore** - Core event infrastructure using NATS JetStream with event sourcing\n- `/app/project/src/module_9.txt` - **Outbox Pattern Implementation** - Reliable event publishing with Ed25519 signatures and NATS broker\n- `/app/project/src/module_12.txt` - **Event Bus Abstraction** - NATS-backed event bus with in-process fan-out and back-pressure awareness\n- `/app/project/src/module_50.txt` - **Outbox Processor** - RabbitMQ/AMQP event publishing with exponential backoff retries\n\n### Domain Services (Write Model)\n- `/app/project/src/module_33.txt` - **PulseService** - Learning Pulse domain with Service/Repository/EventPublisher pattern\n- `/app/project/src/module_60.txt` - **PulseService (Alternative)** - Business logic for creating learning pulses and handling student replies\n- `/app/project/src/module_81.txt` - **LearningPulseService** - Domain model with validation, event generation, and persistence\n\n### Event Consumers (Read Model / CQRS Projections)\n- `/app/project/src/module_15.txt` - **Badge Awarding Service** - Event consumer that awards badges based on domain events\n- `/app/project/src/module_27.txt` - **Search Indexing Service** - Event consumer that indexes pulses into Elasticsearch\n- `/app/project/src/module_20.txt` - **EventDispatcher** - Combines event store persistence with in-process fan-out\n\n### Event Infrastructure (Multiple Broker Support)\n- `/app/project/src/module_64.txt` - **Kafka EventBus** - Kafka-backed event bus with audit trail consumer\n- `/app/project/src/module_72.txt` - **NATS EventPublisher** - Domain event infrastructure with typed events and NATS publishing\n\n### GDPR & Compliance\n- `/app/project/src/module_45.txt` - **GDPR Erasure Service** - Event-sourced user data erasure with soft-delete events\n- `/app/project/src/module_6.txt` - **Audit Event Store** - GDPR-compliant event store with pseudonymization support\n\n---\n\n## Code Evidence\n\n### 1. Authentication & Session Management (module_1.txt)\n\n```rust\n// File: /app/project/src/module_1.txt\n// Lines: 14-27 (Service Description)\n//!\n//! EduPulse Live \u2013 Session-based Authentication Service.\n//!\n//! Responsibilities:\n//! \u25cf Secure user registration (bcrypt password hashing)\n//! \u25cf JWT-based authentication with refresh tokens\n//! \u25cf Session storage in Redis with configurable TTL\n//! \u25cf Role-based access control (RBAC)\n//!\n//! The module exposes an HTTP middleware and a standalone service\n//! that can be used from Axum, Actix-web or any other async framework.\n```\n\n```rust\n// File: /app/project/src/module_1.txt\n// Lines: 133-157 (JWT Authentication)\npub async fn login(\n    &self,\n    email: &str,\n    password_raw: &str,\n) -> Result<AuthResponse, AuthError> {\n    // 1. Find user by email\n    let user = self\n        .repo\n        .find_by_email(email)\n        .await?\n        .ok_or(AuthError::InvalidCredentials)?;\n\n    // 2. Verify password hash (bcrypt)\n    bcrypt::verify(password_raw, &user.password_hash)?;\n\n    // 3. Mint JWT tokens (access + refresh)\n    let access_token = self.mint_access_token(&user)?;\n    let refresh_token = self.mint_refresh_token(&user)?;\n\n    // 4. Create a server-side session in Redis\n    let session = Session::new(user.id, user.role.clone(), self.session_ttl);\n    self.sessions.set(&session).await?;\n\n    Ok(AuthResponse {\n        access_token,\n        refresh_token,\n        session_id: session.id,\n    })\n}\n```\n\n### 2. Event Publishing Infrastructure (module_4.txt)\n\n```rust\n// File: /app/project/src/module_4.txt\n// Lines: 1-20 (Module Description)\n//! src/module_4.rs\n//!\n//! EduPulse Live \u2013 Event-Sourcing Core\n//!\n//! This module provides the building blocks for implementing event-sourced\n//! aggregates and reliable message publishing within the \"EduPulse Live\"\n//! platform.  Key components:\n//!\n//! \u25cf `DomainEvent` \u2013 trait marking an event eligible for persistence/publishing\n//! \u25cf `EventStore` \u2013 trait for persisting events (Postgres implementation)\n//! \u25cf `EventPublisher` \u2013 trait for pushing events to the message bus (NATS impl)\n//! \u25cf `OutboxForwarder` \u2013 worker that drains the \"outbox\" table and publishes\n//!\n//! The design follows the Outbox Pattern to guarantee *exactly-once* delivery\n//! even when the primary DB and the message broker are separate systems.\n```\n\n```rust\n// File: /app/project/src/module_4.txt\n// Lines: 240-268 (NATS JetStream Publisher)\npub struct NatsJsEventPublisher {\n    nc: Arc<nats::asynk::Connection>,\n    jetstream: async_nats::jetstream::Context,\n}\n\nimpl NatsJsEventPublisher {\n    pub async fn connect(url: &str, stream_name: &str) -> Result<Self, PublishError> {\n        let nc = nats::asynk::connect(url)\n            .await\n            .map_err(|e| PublishError::Connection(e.to_string()))?;\n        let js = async_nats::jetstream::new(nc.clone());\n\n        // Ensure stream exists with sensible defaults\n        js.get_or_create_stream(async_nats::jetstream::stream::Config {\n            name: stream_name.to_string(),\n            subjects: vec![format!(\"{stream_name}.>\")],\n            max_age: Duration::from_secs(60 * 60 * 24 * 7), // 7 days\n            ..Default::default()\n        })\n        .await\n        .map_err(|e| PublishError::JetStream(e.to_string()))?;\n\n        Ok(Self {\n            nc: Arc::new(nc),\n            jetstream: js,\n        })\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### 3. Service Layer Pattern (module_33.txt)\n\n```rust\n// File: /app/project/src/module_33.txt\n// Lines: 238-280 (Service Layer)\npub struct PulseService<R: PulseRepository, P: EventPublisher> {\n    repo: R,\n    publisher: P,\n    broker_timeout: Duration,\n}\n\nimpl<R: PulseRepository, P: EventPublisher> PulseService<R, P> {\n    /// Create a Pulse and broadcast a `PulseCreated` domain event.\n    ///\n    /// The method is transactional at the application level. If the event\n    /// cannot be published within [`broker_timeout`], the database insert is\n    /// **not** rolled back (best-effort), but the caller is informed through\n    /// an error.\n    pub async fn create_pulse(&self, new: &NewPulse<'_>) -> Result<LearningPulse, PulseError> {\n        let pulse = self.repo.create(new).await?;\n\n        let event = DomainEvent::PulseCreated(PulseCreated {\n            pulse_id: pulse.id,\n            teacher_id: pulse.teacher_id,\n            occurred_at: Utc::now(),\n        });\n\n        // We don't want to await forever; use `tokio::time::timeout`.\n        timeout(self.broker_timeout, self.publisher.publish(&event))\n            .await\n            .map_err(|_| PulseError::Timeout)??;\n\n        Ok(pulse)\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### 4. Event Consumer Pattern (module_15.txt)\n\n```rust\n// File: /app/project/src/module_15.txt\n// Lines: 1-25 (Event Consumer Service)\n//! src/module_15.rs\n//!\n//! Badge-Awarding Worker\n//! ---------------------\n//! This module implements a background worker that listens to domain events and\n//! awards badges to users when they satisfy certain achievement criteria.  It\n//! showcases:\n//!  \u2022 Event-driven, fully asynchronous architecture\n//!  \u2022 Clean separation of Event-handling / Repository / Service concerns\n//!  \u2022 Structured logging via `tracing`\n//!  \u2022 Strong typing for event payloads\n//!\n//! In production this worker would be deployed as a separate binary or k8s job,\n//! connected to the message broker (NATS / RabbitMQ / Kafka).  For testability\n//! the broker abstraction is hidden behind an `EventConsumer` trait.\n```\n\n```rust\n// File: /app/project/src/module_15.txt\n// Lines: 180-210 (Event Handling Logic)\nasync fn handle_event(\n    &self,\n    envelope: EventEnvelope<'_>,\n) -> Result<(), WorkerError> {\n    match &envelope.payload {\n        DomainEvent::QuizSubmitted {\n            student_id,\n            score,\n            ..\n        } if *score >= 90.0 => {\n            // Award \"Quiz Ace\" badge\n            let badge = Badge::new(\n                *student_id,\n                BadgeKind::QuizAce,\n                \"Scored \u226590% on a quiz\",\n            );\n            self.badge_repo.save(badge).await?;\n            info!(user_id = %student_id, \"Awarded QuizAce badge\");\n        }\n        DomainEvent::PeerFeedbackGiven {\n            reviewer_id, ..\n        } => {\n            // Award \"Helpful Peer\" badge after 5 feedbacks\n            let count = self.badge_repo.count_by_user(*reviewer_id).await?;\n            if count >= 5 {\n                let badge = Badge::new(*reviewer_id, BadgeKind::HelpfulPeer, \"Gave 5+ peer feedbacks\");\n                self.badge_repo.save(badge).await?;\n            }\n        }\n        _ => {}\n    }\n    Ok(())\n}\n```\n\n### 5. CQRS Evidence - Configuration with Multiple DB URLs\n\n```rust\n// File: /app/project/src/config.txt\n// Lines: 63-69 (Database Configuration)\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Deserialize)]\npub struct DatabaseConfig {\n    pub driver: String,\n    pub url: String,\n    pub pool_size: u32,\n}\n```\n\n```yaml\n# File: /app/project/src/config.txt (Example Configuration)\n# Lines: 22-52\ndatabase:\n  driver: \"postgres\"\n  url: \"postgres://epulse:secret@db/edupulse_live\"\n  pool_size: 30\nbroker:\n  host: \"rabbitmq\"\n  port: 5672\n  username: \"mq_user\"\n  password: \"mq_pass\"\n  vhost: \"/edupulse\"\nserver:\n  redis_uri: \"redis://redis:6379\"\n  redis_session_ttl_secs: 86_400\nsearch:\n  elasticsearch_url: \"http://elasticsearch:9200\"\n  index_prefix: \"edupulse_live_\"\n```\n\n---\n\n## Analysis\n\n### 1. Core Architectural Components Identification\n\nBased on comprehensive code analysis, the EduPulse Live platform implements the following architectural patterns:\n\n| Component Role | Module(s) | Evidence |\n|---------------|-----------|----------|\n| **Authentication & Session** | `module_1.txt` | JWT tokens, bcrypt hashing, Redis session store, RBAC |\n| **Event Bus / Message Broker** | `module_4.txt`, `module_12.txt`, `module_64.txt`, `module_72.txt` | NATS JetStream, RabbitMQ (lapin), Kafka (rdkafka) implementations |\n| **Command Handlers (Write Model)** | `module_33.txt`, `module_60.txt`, `module_81.txt` | PulseService with Repository + EventPublisher pattern |\n| **Event Consumers (Read Model)** | `module_15.txt`, `module_27.txt`, `module_20.txt` | Badge awarding, Search indexing, Audit trail consumers |\n| **Outbox Pattern** | `module_9.txt`, `module_50.txt` | Reliable at-least-once event delivery with database-backed outbox |\n| **Event Store** | `module_4.txt`, `module_45.txt`, `module_6.txt` | PostgreSQL event store with append-only semantics |\n\n### 2. Architectural Patterns Identified\n\n#### Event-Driven Architecture (EDA)\nThe system uses an event-driven architecture where domain changes are captured as immutable events and published to a message broker for downstream processing.\n\n**Evidence:**\n- Multiple `EventPublisher` trait implementations (NATS, RabbitMQ, Kafka)\n- `DomainEvent` enums with typed event variants (`PulseCreated`, `QuizSubmitted`, `BadgeAwarded`)\n- Event envelope wrappers with correlation IDs and metadata\n- Asynchronous event consumers for search indexing and badge awarding\n\n#### CQRS (Command Query Responsibility Segregation)\nThe system separates write operations (commands) from read operations (queries), with events bridging the two models.\n\n**Evidence:**\n- Write model: `PulseService` handles commands like `create_pulse()` and persists to primary database\n- Read model: `SearchIndexer` (module_27) maintains Elasticsearch index for optimized queries\n- Event-driven synchronization: Events flow from write services to read model consumers\n- Separate infrastructure: PostgreSQL for writes, Elasticsearch for search queries, Redis for sessions\n\n#### Outbox Pattern\nTo ensure reliable event delivery even when the database and message broker are separate systems, the platform uses the Outbox pattern.\n\n**Evidence from module_9.txt:**\n```rust\n/// Outbox service coordinates persistence and dispatching.\npub struct OutboxService<R: OutboxRepository + Send + Sync> {\n    repo: Arc<R>,\n    nats_url: String,\n    key_pair: Arc<Ed25519KeyPair>,\n}\n\n/// Persists a domain event within an existing transaction.\npub async fn stage_event<E: DomainEvent>(\n    &self,\n    tx: &mut Transaction<'_, Postgres>,\n    aggregate_id: Uuid,\n    event: &E,\n) -> Result<(), OutboxError> {\n    // Event is persisted in the same transaction as the domain change\n    self.repo.insert(tx, &unsigned).await\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Data Flow Analysis: Creating a Post/Pulse in a Study Group\n\nBased on the codebase analysis, here is the complete lifecycle of a user creating a new \"Learning Pulse\" (equivalent to a post in a study group):\n\n### Step-by-Step Flow\n\n1. **API Request (HTTP Layer)**\n   - User sends authenticated POST request to create a pulse\n   - JWT token validated by `module_1.txt` (AuthenticationService)\n   - Session verified against Redis\n\n2. **Command Processing (module_33.txt / module_81.txt)**\n   - `PulseService.create_pulse()` receives the command\n   - Domain validation performed (non-empty title, description)\n   - `LearningPulse` aggregate created with new UUID\n\n3. **Persistence (Repository Layer)**\n   - `PgPulseRepository.create()` inserts record into PostgreSQL\n   - Uses SQLx with compile-time query checking\n\n4. **Event Generation**\n   - `PulseCreated` domain event generated with metadata\n   - Event wrapped in `EventEnvelope` with correlation ID\n\n5. **Event Publishing (module_4.txt / module_9.txt)**\n   - Event staged in outbox table within same transaction (Outbox Pattern)\n   - `OutboxProcessor` polls for unpublished events\n   - Event published to NATS/RabbitMQ with routing key `pulse.created`\n\n6. **Event Consumption (module_27.txt / module_15.txt)**\n   - `SearchIndexer` receives `PulsePublished` event\n   - Fetches full pulse data from repository\n   - Indexes document into Elasticsearch for search queries\n   - Badge service checks if user qualifies for achievements\n\n### Sequence of Modules Involved\n\n```\nClient Request\n    \u2502\n    \u25bc\n[module_1.txt] Authentication/Session Validation\n    \u2502\n    \u25bc\n[module_33.txt or module_81.txt] PulseService.create_pulse()\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500\u25b6 [PostgreSQL] Insert learning_pulses record\n    \u2502\n    \u2514\u2500\u2500\u25b6 [module_9.txt or module_50.txt] Outbox Event Staging\n              \u2502\n              \u25bc\n         [module_4.txt or module_12.txt] Event Publication to NATS/RabbitMQ\n              \u2502\n              \u251c\u2500\u2500\u25b6 [module_27.txt] Search Indexer \u2192 Elasticsearch\n              \u2502\n              \u2514\u2500\u2500\u25b6 [module_15.txt] Badge Worker \u2192 Award badges\n```\n\n---\n\n## Proposed Integration Strategy: Real-time Collaborative Whiteboard\n\n### High-Level Architecture\n\nThe proposed architecture introduces a dedicated **Whiteboard Service** that handles real-time collaboration while integrating seamlessly with the existing event-driven infrastructure.\n\n### New Components Required\n\n#### 1. WebSocket Gateway Service\nA dedicated service for handling low-latency, bidirectional communication.\n\n```rust\n// Proposed: whiteboard_gateway/src/lib.rs\npub struct WhiteboardGateway {\n    sessions: Arc<DashMap<SessionId, WhiteboardSession>>,\n    redis: RedisClient,        // For cross-instance state sync\n    auth_service: AuthClient,  // Validate JWT tokens\n    event_bus: NatsEventBus,   // Integration with core event system\n}\n\nimpl WhiteboardGateway {\n    /// Upgrade HTTP to WebSocket connection\n    pub async fn handle_upgrade(\n        &self,\n        ws: WebSocket,\n        session_id: SessionId,\n        user_token: JwtToken,\n    ) -> Result<(), GatewayError>;\n\n    /// Broadcast drawing action to all session participants\n    pub async fn broadcast_action(\n        &self,\n        session_id: SessionId,\n        action: DrawingAction,\n    ) -> Result<(), GatewayError>;\n}\n```\n\n#### 2. CRDT-based State Management\nFor conflict-free real-time collaboration:\n\n```rust\n// Proposed: whiteboard_crdt/src/lib.rs\npub struct WhiteboardState {\n    /// CRDT for concurrent stroke additions\n    strokes: LWWMap<StrokeId, Stroke>,\n    /// Version vector for causality tracking\n    version: VectorClock,\n    /// Participants currently in session\n    participants: HashSet<UserId>,\n}\n```\n\n#### 3. Persistence Strategy\n\n| Data Type | Storage | Rationale |\n|-----------|---------|-----------|\n| Transient drawing actions | Redis Pub/Sub | Sub-millisecond latency for real-time sync |\n| Session state (active) | Redis Hash | Fast read/write for live collaboration |\n| Whiteboard snapshots | PostgreSQL (JSONB) | Durable storage for session recovery |\n| Completed whiteboards | S3/MinIO (SVG/PNG) | Long-term archival as static assets |\n\n### Integration with Existing Systems\n\n#### Authentication Integration (module_1.txt)\n```rust\n// Reuse existing JWT validation\nasync fn validate_websocket_connection(\n    &self,\n    token: &str,\n) -> Result<AuthenticatedUser, AuthError> {\n    // Call existing AuthenticationService\n    self.auth_service.verify_token(token).await\n}\n```\n\n#### Event Bus Integration (module_4.txt, module_12.txt)\n```rust\n// Publish whiteboard lifecycle events to existing event bus\npub enum WhiteboardEvent {\n    SessionStarted { session_id: Uuid, study_group_id: Uuid, started_by: Uuid },\n    SessionEnded { session_id: Uuid, participant_count: u32, duration_secs: u64 },\n    WhiteboardSaved { session_id: Uuid, storage_url: String },\n}\n\nimpl WhiteboardGateway {\n    async fn publish_session_event(&self, event: WhiteboardEvent) {\n        let envelope = EventEnvelope::new(event);\n        self.event_bus.publish(envelope).await?;\n    }\n}\n```\n\n#### Study Group Integration\n- Whiteboard sessions are scoped to existing Study Groups\n- Permissions derived from study group membership\n- Events trigger notifications to group members\n\n### Data Flow: Real-time Drawing Action\n\n```\nUser draws stroke\n    \u2502\n    \u25bc\n[WebSocket Client] \u2500\u2500\u25ba [Whiteboard Gateway]\n                              \u2502\n                              \u251c\u2500\u2500\u25ba Validate JWT (module_1 integration)\n peers (Redis Pub/Sub)\n                              \u2502\n                              \u2514\u2500\u2500\u25ba Debounced snapshot to PostgreSQL\n```\n\n---\n\n## Architectural Diagrams\n\n### Layer\"\n        A[React + WASM Client]\n        A1[Whiteboard Canvas Component]\n    end\n\n    subgraph \"API Layer\"\n        B[HTTP API Gateway]\n        C[module_1: AuthenticationService]\n        W1[WebSocket Gateway - NEW]\n    end\n\n    subgraph \"Whiteboard Service - NEW\"\n        W2[WhiteboardSessionManager]\n        W3[CRDT State Engine]\n        W4[SnapshotService]\n    end\n\n    subgraph \"Service Layer - Write Model\"\n        D[module_33: PulseService]\n        E[PulseRepository]\n    end\n\n    subgraph \"Event Infrastructure\"\n        F[module_9: OutboxService]\n Event| G\n    H -->|Subscribe whiteboard.*| W5\n    W5 -->|Index Sessions| L\n```\n\n---\n\n## Architectural Risks and Mitigations\n\n### Risk 1: WebSocket Session Statefulness and Horizontal Scaling\n\n**Description:**\nUnlike the existing stateless HTTP services, WebSocket connections are inherently stateful. A user's WebSocket connection is tied to a specific server instance. If multiple gateway instances exist (for high availability), participants in the same whiteboard session may be connected to different servers, requiring cross-instance synchronization.\n\n**Impact:**\n- Session affinity required for load balancing\n- Increased complexity for failover handling\n- Potential message loss during server restarts\n- Higher memory usage per instance\n\n**Mitigation:**\n1. **Redis Pub/Sub for Cross-Instance Sync:** Use Redis Pub/Sub channels keyed by session ID to broadcast drawing actions across all gateway instances.\n2. **Sticky Sessions with Health Checks:** Configure load balancer with WebSocket-aware sticky sessions, but implement reconnection logic that can migrate to healthy instances.\n3. **Session State in Redis:** Store authoritative CRDT state in Redis, treating gateway instances as stateless relays. This allows any instance to serve any session.\n4. **Graceful Degradation:** Implement client-side conflict resolution using CRDTs so that temporary network partitions don't cause data loss.\n\n### Risk 2: Real-time Performance vs. Event Bus Latency Mismatch\n\n**Description:**\nThe existing event bus (NATS/RabbitMQ) is designed for eventual consistency with acceptable latencies of 50-500ms. Real-time collaborative drawing requires sub-20ms latency for a smooth user experience. Using the event bus for drawing actions would create a poor user experience.\n\n**Impact:**\n- Perceived lag in collaborative drawing\n- Potential for high message volume overwhelming the event bus\n- Out-of-order stroke rendering causing visual artifacts\n\n**Mitigation:**\n1. **Dual-Path Communication:**\n   - **Hot path (Real-time):** Use direct WebSocket broadcast via Redis Pub/Sub for drawing actions. This bypasses the event bus entirely for transient data.\n   - **Cold path (Persistence):** Use the existing event bus for lifecycle events (SessionStarted, SessionEnded, WhiteboardSaved) that integrate with analytics and audit systems.\n\n2. **Local-First Rendering:** Apply optimistic updates on the client immediately. The client renders strokes locally before confirmation, masking network latency.\n\n3. **Batch Compression:** Instead of publishing each mouse movement, batch coordinates into polyline segments (e.g., every 50ms) to reduce message frequency by 10-20x while maintaining visual fidelity.\n\n### Risk 3: Data Consistency Between Real-time State and Persistent Storage\n\n**Description:**\nThe whiteboard feature introduces a tension between real-time collaboration (ephemeral, in-memory state) and durable persistence (database snapshots). If snapshots are taken too infrequently, a server crash could lose significant user work. If taken too frequently, it creates excessive database load.\n\n**Impact:**\n- Potential data loss on server failure\n- Database write amplification from frequent snapshots\n- Inconsistent state between what users see and what's persisted\n- Recovery complexity after crashes\n\n**Mitigation:**\n1. **Incremental Operation Log:** Instead of full snapshots, persist the CRDT operation log (append-only). This provides point-in-time recovery with minimal I/O.\n\n2. **Tiered Persistence Strategy:**\n   - **Level 1 (1s):** Write operation log to Redis with 1-hour TTL\n   - **Level 2 (30s):** Compress and checkpoint to PostgreSQL\n   - **Level 3 (Session End):** Generate final SVG/PNG and store in S3\n\n3. **Write-Ahead Logging:** Similar to database WAL, log all operations before acknowledgment. On recovery, replay the log to reconstruct state.\n\n4. **Optimistic Acknowledgment:** Acknowledge user actions after Redis write (Level 1), not after PostgreSQL commit. Provide visual feedback for \"auto-saved\" status.\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\n- **Primary Finding:** EduPulse Live is a well-architected event-driven platform following CQRS and event-sourcing patterns. The modular design with trait-based abstractions for `EventPublisher`, `Repository`, and `EventBus` enables clean integration of the proposed whiteboard feature.\n\n- **Key Components Identified:**\n  - `module_1.txt` - Authentication & Session Management (JWT + Redis)\n  - `module_4.txt`, `module_9.txt` - Event Publishing Infrastructure (Outbox Pattern + NATS)\n  - `module_33.txt`, `module_81.txt` - Domain Service Layer (Command Handlers)\n  - `module_15.txt`, `module_27.txt` - Event Consumers (Read Model Projections)\n\n- **Architectural Patterns:**\n  - **Event-Driven Architecture (EDA)** - Asynchronous event publishing via NATS/RabbitMQ/Kafka\n  - **CQRS** - Separate write (PostgreSQL) and read (Elasticsearch) models\n  - **Outbox Pattern** - Reliable at-least-once event delivery\n  - **Repository Pattern** - Abstracted data access with async traits\n\n- **Proposed Integration:**\n  - **WebSocket Gateway** for sub-20ms real-time communication\n  - **CRDT-based state management** for conflict-free collaboration\n  - **Dual-path architecture:** Redis Pub/Sub for hot path, existing event bus for cold path\n  - **Tiered persistence:** Redis \u2192 PostgreSQL \u2192 S3 for reliability/performance balance\n\n- **Critical Risks:**\n  1. Stateful WebSocket scaling \u2192 Mitigate with Redis-backed state externalization\n  2. Latency mismatch \u2192 Mitigate with dedicated real-time path separate from event bus\n  3. Consistency challenges \u2192 Mitigate with operation logging and tiered persistence\n\nThe existing architecture's emphasis on trait-based abstractions and event-driven communication provides an excellent foundation for integrating real-time collaborative features while maintaining the system's reliability and scalability characteristics.\n",
  "file_path": "/logs/agent/solution.md"
